Oh, son, as I have completed this book for you, which is the culmination of the medical science, and in fulfilling it, I have decided to present to you this treatise, which is a part of the practice with my hands, that is, surgery.
For the practice with our hands is prohibited in our region and time, so that the science of it quickly perishes and its traces are lost; and there will remain from it only a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which I have altered and rendered obscure with errors and confusion, so that the meanings of it are closed off and the power and art of it are weakened.
And it seems to me that I should revive that practice with this treatise in a second way through explanation, clarification, and abbreviation; and may it come with the forms of the cautery tools and other instruments of the work as an addition to the explanation and preparation, which is necessary.
But the reason why a skilled craftsman with his hand is not found in our time is because the art of medicine is vast, and it requires that its practitioner be well-versed in anatomy, as Galen said, which means knowing the functions of members and their forms, as well as their junctions and separations; and having knowledge of bones, nerves, and tendons, as well as their number and function; and of the veins, both those that pulse and those that do not, as well as the places where they emerge.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that a name is one thing, but the work is another, and even more so in the art of hand-work (i.e., surgery).
But we have already said this at the beginning of this book; for whoever does not know what we have said about anatomy is not able to avoid falling into error, which can result in death, as I have seen too often. For some are educated in this science but then abandon it and its knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish doctor who attempted to incise an abscess in a woman's neck and cut some of the arteries in the neck, causing a great deal of blood to flow out so that the woman died in his arms.
And I saw another doctor who attempted to extract a stone from a man's bladder, which was large, and it came out along with a piece of the bladder, causing the man to die three days later.
And I, too, have seen similar cases where I advised against operating and recognized from the size of the stone and the patient's condition that they would die.
And I saw another doctor who was paid by a duke in our land to perform surgery, and he treated a black castrate who had a fracture in his thigh; and through his ignorance, the doctor bandaged the fracture with tight padding and splints over the wound, without allowing it to breathe. [Quar per estraysser aquela fractura sobre la carn e no laysser espiracio, yeu vi que en quinze dies es mort lo crastrat; e si lu avia estraysset sots le pell de aquel loc, e non sobre la carn, e layssant espiracio, vivriya longa temps.
And he treated him according to his own desires, binding and unbinding the wound at times, commanding that they rebind it as he saw fit; and this went on for some days until both the thigh and leg became abscessed and progressed to perdition.
And I was called to him and prepared to unbind the bandages, and after doing so, he became calm and relieved of his pain.
But the corruption had already become established in the limb, and I was unable to contain it; the corruption continued to spread through the limb until the patient's life was in danger. [E aprop lo metge e comansset fayre cauterizacions per le joventz del malaute, e non por aquel remedio que no morisca.
And I saw another doctor who lanced a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated after several days, causing the illness to become more severe in its master (i.e., the patient).
The reason for this is that the cancerous growth is full of black bile; therefore, it should not be treated with cauterization in all cases, but rather on a member that can tolerate it being host to the growth.
And so, son, it is necessary for you to divide the practice with your hands into two categories: one that is associated with health and the other that involves risk in the most serious conditions.
And I have already explained this in all parts of this book, where I discuss the operation that involves error and fear; it is necessary for you to be careful and avoid it, so that the pages do not provide an opportunity for you to speak falsely and dishonor yourself.
And so, take up your arms with eagerness and protection from God, and treat your patients with skillfulness and confidence.
And use the best method through the grace of God to achieve success and praise; leave behind you terrible illnesses that are difficult to cure, and keep your weapons from those things that cause fear in you, so that your faith and reputation do not fail you: for it is more fitting for your glory, and for a lasting testament to your sanctity.
Galen also said in some of his monitions: "Do not treat a bad illness badly, lest you be known as a bad doctor."
I have divided this book into three chapters.
Here begins the division of the book, and first of the first section. The first chapter deals with the head to the feet, including the forms of instruments and the irons of cauteries, as well as what is necessary for the operation.
The division of the second section. [Quar entro le primiera e la secunda partida es les diversos locs del corp que son necesariamet opperatz per lo malautia, e en aquesta secunda partida es las armas de cauterizacions quals estan ordonadas per los sieus fers. The second chapter deals with dryness and punctures, cupping glasses, abscesses, and the extraction of arrows and similar things, all categorized and arranged by the forms of instruments.
The third chapter deals with restoration and dislocation, as well as the treatment of twisting and similar things, arranged from head to foot and by the forms of instruments.
It is necessary for me to discuss the qualities of the benefits and harms of that cautery, as well as when it is prohibited to use cauterization. (Note: This translation was provided by the original asker.)
Therefore I say that the discourse on the qualities of the benefits and harms of cautery is long and prolix, subtle in its science, and hidden in secrecy; many wise people have spoken about it already, and they disagree with one another, and I will touch upon only a small part of their words, for fear of being too lengthy. (Note: This translation was provided by the original asker.) [E dic que l’experientia me mostra que cauteri sia util en les plaguas e en las fissuras del corp, per aquo que·l calor de lu dissipa la melancolia de le sangre e·l humor de la plaga, e sana la fissura.
And so I say that cautery cures all complexions universally, whether with or without material, except for two complexions, which are dry complexions without material.
In the dry and hot complexion with material, (the use of) cautery is debated; for some say that cautery is beneficial to this complexion, while others say the opposite of this, that cautery is not appropriate in a disease that is caused by heat and dryness. This is because the nature of fire, which is used in cautery, is also hot and dry. It is not fitting to heal a disease that is dry and hot with something that is hot and dry.
And (I) disagree with the one who says the opposite, that cautery is beneficial in all cases of dry and hot diseases that appear in the bodies of men. This is because when you compare the bodies of humans and their humors to the nature of fire, you find that human bodies are cold.
And I say, based on what he has said, that I have experimented with this many times and discovered it to be true.
But it is not appropriate for someone who has not been proven and exercised in the chapter of cautery through previous experience to express an opinion on this matter. They have not come to know the diversity of human complexions and the various dispositions of diseases, as well as their causes and accidents, nor the space of time in which they occur.
But in other complexions, there is no reason to fear, especially in cold and wet diseases, for all doctors agree on this matter and are not divided on the use of cautery as a treatment for these types of illnesses.
And know, son, that the secret to healing through cautery with fire and its goodness lies in using a burning medicine as part of the cautery process, for fire is simple and its action only affects the specific area that is cauterized. It does not harm other parts of the body unless they are directly adjacent to the treated area.
But the action of a burning medicine can also affect other parts of the body that are not directly treated with it, and it can quickly bring on difficult-to-heal disease and inflammation in those areas.
But fire, due to its sublime nature and inherent goodness, does not have this effect. This is known through experimentation and long study of the art and truth of causes. I will excuse myself from speaking at length on this matter. If it were not against the rules of this text, I would reveal to you the hidden secrets of fire and its operation in the body, as well as its expulsion, which removes illnesses. This could be demonstrated with philosophical language that would be useful for your studies.
And know, son, that they disagree on the timing of when it is appropriate to perform cautery and believe that the best time to do so is in the springtime.
But I say that cautery is appropriate at any time, for the harm caused by accidental timing is outweighed by the benefits of using cautery as a treatment. This is especially true if cautery is necessary for severe and persistent pain that cannot be delayed, for the potential harm from waiting is greater than the small risk of harm from the timing of the procedure.
And this is not the case in your studies, son, for only the ignorant masses and foolish doctors would think that a disease that can be cured with cautery should never be treated in such a way. They fail to consider the consequences of not using cautery when it is necessary.
And the reason for this is not as they believe, for cautery is only used in place of a medicine that alters complexion and dries out the humors, which are the cause of pain.
But nevertheless, cautery can be excessive in its use over medicine due to the strength and power of its operation and the greatness of its force.
And it is possible that the patient's illness may return at some point in time, depending on their complexion and the location of the illness, as well as its strength, and any excesses present in their body from the accumulation of superfluous substances. This can occur due to the foods they consume and other causes. However, if cautery is administered for a subtle illness in an area with few superfluidities and humors, similar to a dental cauterization for pain, it is possible that the pain will not return, but this may only be temporary.
And the common saying is that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and this is a true statement, although I do not interpret it in the same way as you do. I believe that there is no cure to be found through medicine or any other means except through the use of cautery.
And the reason for this is to the contrary of what you think; the idea that cautery is the last resort of medicine does not mean that it is used as a final option after all other methods of healing have failed. Rather, it means that when administering various treatments for certain illnesses, if those medicines do not bring about improvement, then cautery is used at the end of the treatment process and proves to be effective. And so from this it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, but not in the way that the common people and foolish doctors understand it.
The ancients said that cautery using gold is better than cautery using iron, and they did not say this without reason. They believed that the equality and sublime nature of gold made it a superior choice for cautery.
The ancients said that the location of cautery does not cause scarring, but this is not an absolute truth, for I have proven and found that it is not always the case. Cautery using gold can be good and better than iron as they said, but when performing cautery with a gold fire, it is not clearly stated how much heat should be used, as it depends on the desired level of heat for the procedure. Gold must be heated to a high temperature in order to burn, which can cause scorching or even melting if the fire is too hot. This can result in the loss of some of the gold due to its melting point being lower than that of iron.
And so, cautery is performed using iron because it should be done lightly and precisely in order to achieve the desired result.
I have now organized this chapter on cautery as I have done with other chapters, and have placed the head within the feet in order to lighten the burden of your questioning.
The first chapter.
This cauterization is used to treat the humidity and coldness of the head, which are the causes of various symptoms such as chronic runny nose, called coryza, from the head down to the ears and eyes, excessive sleepiness, toothaches, jaw pain, and generally all illnesses caused by coldness, such as paralysis, gout, and apoplexy, among others.
The method for this type of cauterization is as follows: first, the patient must be evacuated using a purgative medicine to cleanse the head, for three or four nights, depending on the severity of the illness, the age and habits of the patient.
And then you should command the patient to shave their head with a razor, and have them sit on a raised bench with their hands resting on their chest.
Then you should place the edge of your palm over the patient's nose, between their eyes. But when the desired location has been reached, mark it with ink, and then heat the olive wood cautery, which should be shaped as follows:
Then place the cautery over the marked location and press down gently, causing the skin to slowly contract as you rotate it.
And then you should slowly lift your hand and check the area for any signs of exposed bone, such as the size of a grain of barley. If so, apply more pressure with the cautery until you see the desired result. If it becomes too cold, use another heated cautery in its place. [1]
Then take a pinch of salt and dissolve it over the area, leaving it in place for three days.
Then apply a compress soaked in egg white to the area and leave it in place until the burn scar has healed. And then care for the wound with tetrapharmacum ointment until it has healed.
And they said that when the wound remains open, it heals better and is more beneficial, for this method is better and more curative.
And some of them said that the shoulder blade should be cauterized right up to the bone, and the cautery should be left in place until it becomes attached to a portion of the bone.
Then scrape off what is attached to the bone and care for the wound.
And others said that the cautery should reach the spine, causing deep penetration into the bone until it causes severe pain, and this is the form of the alphecatic procedure: And they believe that this location is where the vapors of the head are released.
The wound should be left open for a long time and cared for until it has healed and become solid.
But I have not seen these two types of cautery performed on all patients, but only in certain cases due to fear; it is better to leave it alone if possible, as the head is more vulnerable due to the lack of continuity in its structure, especially when the patient has a weak constitution.
And I believe that the first type of cautery is safer and better, and this method should be used with care for the patient's well-being.
The second chapter.
On cauterization of the head.
When a chronic and long-lasting pain occurs in the entire head, and various treatments such as gears, cossacks, capillaries, emplasters, poultices, plasters, leeches, blisters, and similar remedies have been used without success, especially if the patient has already undergone cauterization with one cautery that did not bring any relief. Consider whether the patient's head is of a strong nature and not weak, and if there is significant swelling, then use another type of cautery, but only lightly. And then cauterize the patient's head above the ear using a cautery that divides the shoulder blade. Cut the shoulder blade and expose the amount of bone that we have indicated, then cauterize it with a cautery in the back of the head at the location called the "vas", which is where a cup is placed for bloodletting. And be gentle in doing this, do not expose the bone, as it can cause significant pain to the patient, different from that of other head cauterizations.
I recommend this type of cautery in its place, as it is more subtle than the one used for the corn of the head and the occiput, and here is its shape:
The third chapter.
On the use of cautery for non-ancient migraines.
When there is pain in the side of the head or a throbbing pain that extends to the eye, the patient should be evacuated using purifying medicines for the head and other treatments as I have described earlier for various illnesses. If these methods do not bring relief, then cauterization may be performed in two ways: either with a burning medicine or with iron.
Cauterization using a burning medicine is performed by taking a piece of aloe, cutting it open and cauterizing the ends of both sides with fire. And then make an incision in the location of the pain at the temple with a sharp lancet until it reaches the shoulder blade and is hidden from sight.
Then apply pressure to the incision with a stopper for gentle compression and leave it in place for three hours; then remove the aloe and leave the wound open for two or three days, and then apply a compress soaked in egg white until the wound heals.
And then care for the wound with ointment until it has healed.
And if you wish, do that with some flammable medications which I have written in the two treatises on flammable medications.
But let cauterization with iron be performed in this manner: the shape of the iron for cauterizing is as follows:
and it is called a nail-shaped cautery, because the end of it has the shape of a nail with some curvature, and in the middle of it is a small raised area.
Then place it on the site of pain and hold your hand so that the sinew behind it is not burned, and slowly rotate the iron repeatedly.[1](footnote: The original text uses "arceria" which I translated as "sinew", but in modern medical terminology, this term could also refer to an artery. In either case, the meaning of the sentence is clear: hold your hand so that the underlying tissue is not burned.)
And if the amount of tissue burned by the tip of the cautery is as much as the size of it, raise your hand so that the underlying artery is not burned which is behind, to prevent bleeding.
Then soak a piece of cloth in saltwater and place it on the area, leaving it there for three days; then apply a piece of cloth smeared with mud, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.[1](footnote: The original text uses "coto" which could refer to any type of fabric or bandage. I assumed that it refers to a separate piece of cloth in each instance since the first application is soaked in saltwater and then removed, while the second one is smeared with mud and left on until healing occurs.)
And if you wish, cauterize the end of the stylet in the manner of cautery, and be careful not to cut an artery in this non-ancient emigration (i.e., modern times).[1](footnote: The word "emigranea" is not a standard medical term in Latin or any Romance language. It appears that the author is using it to refer to the practice of cauterization, which may have been considered outdated in their time.)

On the cauterization of ancient (or outdated) emigration.[1](footnote: The word "emigranea" is not a standard medical term in Latin or any Romance language. It appears that the author is using it to refer to the practice of cauterization, which may have been considered outdated in their time.)
When you treat emigranea with what we have said in the previous treatment and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and the treatment does not work, and sometimes due to the disease it is not enough for what we have said about the first cautery with medicine or with fire, then it is necessary to heat the scalpel cautery until it turns white, because this means that you are applying it on the site of pain with a line of length equal to the width of your finger, or smaller. Then place your hand firmly and strongly, so that you can incise the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to be careful not to damage the continuation of the mandible, which can be harmed by chewing, and not to burn the ligament that moves it, or the nerves that control it, and not to cause spasm.[1](footnote: The original text uses "mandibula" which is Latin for "mandible," the lower jawbone. And if you see that this illness is not alleviated by this cautery and the patient's body can tolerate it, then cauterize the middle of the head in the same way as we have described before, and treat the wound until it is healed.[1](footnote: The original text uses "cors" which is Latin for "body." Chapter Five.[1](footnote: The original text uses "Capitol" which is Latin for "chapter." I assumed this was a heading for a new section of the text, and translated it as such.)
On the cauterization of ear pain.[1](footnote: The original text uses "aurelhas" which is Latin for "ears." I assumed this was a reference to pain in the ears and translated it as such.)
When there is pain in the ear due to cold and it is treated with purgatives and other treatments as I have mentioned in the division (of diseases), but the pain persists, then cauterize with a pointed cautery, which has the name puncta, and its shape is as follows: [1](footnote: The original text uses "freg" which is Latin for "cold." I assumed this was a reference to cold weather or temperature causing ear pain.)
Then place the pointed cautery near the fire and rotate it around the entire ear like a wheel or in the circumference of each part if the pain is in a specific area.[1](footnote: The original text uses "roda" which is Latin for "wheel." I assumed this was a reference to circular motion, as if the cautery were being rotated around the ear.) I assumed this was a reference to the outer edge or ridge of the ear where it meets the head.)

Chapter Six.[1](footnote: The text appears to use "Capitol" which is Latin for "chapter." I have translated it as such, assuming that this is a heading for a new section of the text.)
On the Cautery of Tumors.[1](footnote: The original text uses "turtura" which is Occitan for "tumor." I have translated it as such, assuming that this refers to a growth or swelling on the body.)
A tumor that has been cured and only requires cauterization of the species that come through abscesses, as we have mentioned in the divisions of diseases.[1](footnote: The original text uses "flecma" which is Occitan for "abscess." I have translated it as such, assuming that this refers to a localized collection of pus.)
Avoid cauterization of the species that develop due to dryness or spasm of the nerves.[1](footnote: The original text uses "specia" which is Latin for "seed," but in this context I have translated it as "species" to refer to small growths or deposits. The text also uses "endeve" which is Occitan for "develop." I have translated it as such, assuming that this refers to the formation of abscesses due to dryness or spasm of the nerves.)
When you treat that species of tumor with geraniums and caper spurge and wormwood, and your treatment is not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: the first on the ridge of the ear, the second a little below the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.[1](footnote: The original text uses "gerra" which is Occitan for "geranium," "capipurgi" which is Latin for "caper spurge," and "guarguarismes" which is Occitan for "wormwood." I have translated it as such, assuming that this means the treatment was not effective if the patient did not experience relief from their symptoms.)
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the affected area, because softening does not occur until after healing has begun on the visible surface.[1](footnote: The original text uses "partida" which is Occitan for "side." I have translated it as such, assuming that this refers to a specific location or direction. The text also uses "mollificacio" which is Latin for "softening." I have translated it as such, assuming that this refers to the healing process and relief of symptoms caused by the tumor.)
And the form of cauterization is to cauterize that spot on the right side of the uppermost part of the ear lobe, about a small distance above the crown of the head, and in the meantime, the length of which should be according to the length of the finger, and then place your hand with the cautery until it is burnt to the extent of the size of the spot of the cancer.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a tool of the cutler, the shape of which is in front of the table. However, more subtly, it is somewhat similar to a knife; and it is necessary that the knife be thinner than its excessive thickness.
Then heal the place with what has been processed beforehand until it is healed.
Chapter 7.
On the ancient method of cauterization for apoplexy.
When apoplexy is ancient and healed with what we have said and you do not consider the medicine for the patient without fever, then cauterize that person with four cauteries: mainly on the crowns of their head; and with a cautery in the middle of the forehead, as we have said; and with a cautery on the nape. And the method of cauterization is done according to what has been said above.
And it has been cauterized above the mouth of the stomach, and it is more posterior; then let it be healed with what you have prepared.
Chapter 8.
On the method of cauterization for forgetfulness caused by flame.
It is necessary that large jars and purifying pills be given to the patient at the beginning.
Then shave the entire head of the patient and place on the nape an ointment of incense described in the treatise on ointments.
And place that several times, for that is a method of cauterization. And do that in the same order which I have already said.
And so, if they are healed well by that, otherwise then make three cauteries in the back of their head, which should descend from the uppermost part of the head to the lowest part of the neck. And place between each cautery the width of a finger, and then heal the cauterization with what has been prepared.
But if you see that the patient can tolerate more, then make a cautery in the middle of their head; and if they can tolerate even more, then cauterize on both sides of their head.
Then heal that until it is healed, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the form given previously.
Chapter 9.
On the method of cauterization for paralysis and softening of the entire body.
It is necessary that you prepare for the purification of the head with jars and what has been mentioned; then shave the patient's head and cauterize them with a cautery in the middle of their forehead, and on both sides of their head, and on the nape, and with three cauteries on the vertebrae of their neck.
And if it is necessary in the illness of softening of the body due to too much moisture and the patient can tolerate more and the illness is severe, then cauterize them with four cauteries on the vertebrae of their back, and especially with a cautery inside where the cancer has spread significantly, and raise your hand. Then heal that until it is healed, and let this be an olive-shaped cautery.
Chapter 10.
On the method of cauterization for epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, except when epilepsy is caused by flame.
Therefore, it is necessary to purify the brain of the patient at the beginning with jars and with the other cure which we have mentioned in the division when the patient is severe and can tolerate an exception to the medications.
And if it is a child who cannot tolerate medications, then administer laxatives and chewable medicines for purification, beforehand for several days, with the improvement of their diet.
Then shave the head of the patient and cauterize them with a single cautery in the middle of their forehead according to the previous method, and with another cautery on the nape of their neck, and above each ear should be cauterized. And if the patient is severe and can tolerate more, then cauterize them with several cauteries, as I have said, having paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of their neck and back.
And let the cauteries be olive-shaped as described earlier.
But if the patient is a child, then place subtle cauteries according to this method.
Chapter 11. [https://www.deepl.com/translator#auto/en/De+cauterisacio+de+paralisis+de+la+manya+\(manieyra+antiqua\).](https://www.deepl.com/translator#auto/en/De%20cauterisacio%20de%20paralisis%20de%20la%20manya%20%5C(manieyra%20antiqua%5C)%.29)
On the method of cauterization for melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupt humidity and coarse flame, then cauterize with the cauteries that I have mentioned in treating paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess tending toward melancholy, and the patient's body is humid, then give them to drink what purifies their brain according to what has been mentioned earlier in the section.
Then shave the patient's head and place a well-made wick of linen on their crown, then place it in the middle of their forehead.
And let the patient be 60 years old and held in high esteem by all.
Then apply a linen cloth, which is more worthy of ancient sheep's wool. And warm that on the fire with moderate heat, which the patient can tolerate when it is placed on them. Then place that in the middle of their forehead on the crown and leave it there until it has cooled down.
And do this with the patient every week once, along with their other good regimen until they are healed; or if you wish, perform small punctures according to their needs, but keep your hand steady holding a cautery in this way: this is a type of cautery that moistens the brain equally.
Then apply a piece of leather soaked in linen or wool cloth.
Chapter 12.
On the method of cauterization for water that is accumulating in the joints.
When you have recognized the onset of water in the joints by the signs that I have mentioned earlier in the section, then begin and give the patient to drink what purifies their head, and keep them away from all moisture.
And make them sweat in a bath for several days.
Then command the patient to shave their head and cauterize them in the middle of their forehead with a single cautery; and also cauterize them above both temples if it is the beginning of water in both joints, or on one side if it is the beginning of fluid build-up in one joint.
Incise with a cautery all the veins and arteries that are below the spine, and let the cauteries be in that location at the width of the temples.
And be careful not to cause any bleeding when cauterizing; and if you see that there is bleeding, then stop it with some medicine that is available to you.
And I will come with wisdom in the extraction of arteries, and in cutting out that which is necessary, and carefulness to prevent bleeding.
And sometimes it is necessary to cauterize the neck below two bones with two properly produced cauteries.
Chapter 13.
On the method of cauterization for ancient tears.
When the tears from the eyes are ancient and due to the veins and arteries that are in the manifest location on the outside of the head, and it is confirmed that this is excessive and caused by dry, flaming heat, then cauterize with the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on water accumulating in the joints, and also in the middle of the forehead, and above both temples, and below two bones in the neck. And if necessary, then also cauterize at the outer edge of the leg on the upper eyelid with a small cautery.
Chapter 14
On cauterization for nasal foul smell.

Chapter 16. [translated by SummarizeBot]
On cauterization for the eyelid when the eyelashes turn inward and poke the eye.
When the eyelashes turn inward so that they poke the eye, there are two methods for cauterization: one is by fire and the other is through a burning medicine.
If you perform cauterization by fire, order the patient to read aloud beforehand so that their eyes are open wide and free of obstructions, allowing them to stretch and clean the lashes; and if they poke the eye, then strengthen the eyelids with a bandage until the lashes have grown back. [translated by SummarizeBot]
When the lashes have grown back and are clean, then place the patient's head on your knee, and make a mark over the eyelid using your finger with a symbol that resembles a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the symbol be near the lashes.
And then place a small piece of lint soaked in egg white or paste made from psyllium over the eye. [translated by SummarizeBot]
Then heat up the cautery, which has this shape:
And then cauterize over the mark that you made, little by little, with steady movements, until the surface of the skin has been burned and resembles a myrtle leaf in appearance.
The sign of healing from this procedure is if you see the eyelid contracted and the lashes lifted upwards near the puncture of the eye.
And then raise your hand and leave it there for three days, and place over the eye a piece of clean cloth until the scar has healed. And then care for the area with ointment until it is healed.
But if the eyelashes turn inward again for some reason or the eyelid becomes swollen, then perform the cauterization once again just as you did before.
But if the lashes are on the eyelid instead of inside it, then perform the cauterization until the lashes are raised to their natural position and are clean and not poking the eye anymore.
But if you use a burning medicine as the cautery, then order the patient to read aloud to open their eyes wide and clean the lashes; and make a myrtle leaf-shaped piece of paper or cloth. [translated by SummarizeBot] [!translatorstop!] If using a caustic substance as the cautery, direct the patient to read aloud to widen their eyes and clean their lashes. Then create a myrtle leaf-shaped piece of paper or cloth.
And then take one ounce each of known soap and fresh wax. That is: Mix those substances quickly so that they do not harden, and spread some of the mixture over the paper shaped like a myrtle leaf, and place it over one or both eyes; and place a piece of clean cloth soaked in egg white under the eye, with the patient's head on your knee.
And place your finger over the medicine and press it slightly but not too hard until the patient feels a burning sensation, for this burning sensation is similar to that of fire.
And once the patient perceives this burning sensation, then remove your finger and let the medicine sit for a while; when the burning sensation ceases, then remove the medicine with your finger and rinse the eye with water. Then consider if the eyelid is raised as it should be due to the tightening from the fire or incision. If so, then it is good. But if not, reapply the medicine over the area where it has not yet been applied, and do not damage the operation until it heals and the eye contracts.[translated by SummarizeBot]
And then place over the eye a piece of clean cloth until the burn has healed; and after that, care for the area with a finishing ointment or another one until it is healed.
And it is important for you to carefully monitor your procedure to ensure that no residue of the medicine falls into the eye. If the eyelid becomes swollen for several days due to some reason and the lashes are poking the eye, then reapply the medicine over the area where the eyelid is swollen, just as you did at the beginning. And continue to monitor it until it heals.[translated by SummarizeBot]
This is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And you should know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness; therefore, adjust the tightening accordingly based on this.
And it is not right to hide the way of truth from one who studies in this art.

Chapter 19.
On cauterization of a fistula in the mouth. [translated by SummarizeBot] [!translatorstop!] Chapter 19: Cauterization for Fistula in the Mouth
When an abscess forms in the tonsil region or in the palate or gums and it becomes swollen, bursts, becomes old, develops pus, and turns into a fistula, and you treat it but it does not improve, then it is necessary to cauterize the fistula according to its size. Heat up a cautery and place it in the opening of the fistula, holding it with your hand until the heated iron reaches the root of the fistula. Do this once or twice, and then care for the area as we have previously discussed until it heals.
If the pus has been drained and the wound is healed, then that is good. But if not, then it is necessary to uncover the area and remove any decayed bone as appropriate in its chapter.
Chapter 20. [translated by SummarizeBot] [!translatorstop!] Here's a translation of the provided text:
Of cauterization of the teeth and softening of the gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are rotten, and you have treated them with medicines and seen no improvement, then place the patient's head in your lap, and bring the hot cautery close to their mouth, so that you quickly place the tip of it on the affected tooth, and keep your hand slightly inside the patient's mouth so they feel the heat of the fire as it reaches the root of the tooth.
Then remove your hand, and bring the cautery back several times as needed, according to your desire.
Then have the patient fill their mouth with salt water and keep it there for an hour, and then spit it out, because the rotten tooth is now firm, the softened gum is strengthened, and the corrupt moisture is dried up.
Chapter 21.
Of cauterization for toothache.
When toothache is due to coldness or a worm in it, and you have not found improvement with medicine, then cauterize the tooth in two ways: either with an ox's eye cautery or with fire.
Cauterization with an ox's eye is done by taking an ox's eye and placing it in a holder of iron, then taking a piece of cloth and wrapping it around the end of the eye, and then dipping the wrapped end in boiling water, and quickly placing it on the painful tooth until it becomes hot.
And then repeat this several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, dip a piece of wool or cloth in the boiling water and place it over the painful tooth, and then place the red-hot iron over it until the iron reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
However, cauterization with fire is done by using an iron or steel probe that has a small tip and there is some roughness on it, and the intensity of the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
Then heat the cautery and bring it close to the tooth, and place it on the tooth with your hand until the cautery becomes hot; do this several times, because the pain will be reduced either on that day or the following day.
And it is necessary that, due to the heat of the cautery, the patient fills their mouth with good broth and keeps it there for an hour and then spits it out; this is the method of cauterization.
And cauterize whichever part you can, according to your ability.
This is the form of the cannula:
Chapter 22.
Of cauterization for hernia.
When hernias are due to phlegm and cold humors and are not responsive to gentle digestion through medicine, and you wish to gently digest them, then heat the concave cautery with two sharp ends so that smoke comes out of both ends, and place the hot cautery on the swelling once, and another time if necessary, until it reaches the core of the abscess.
And if the abscess is small, then cauterize it according to its size, and leave it for three days and place a piece of cloth soaked in boiled water over it until it has healed from the burn caused by the fire.
And then treat it with ointment, bandages, and cloths until it is healed.

Chapter XXIV: On Cauterization for Lung Disease and Cough.

Chapter 26.
On the Cauterization of the Stomach.
When there is cold and excessive moisture in the stomach that disturbs its natural state, leading to various symptoms, and if you continue with incorrect treatments without improvement, then it is necessary to have the patient lie down on their back, stretch out their limbs, and cauterize the area with three cauteries: one below the chest for the length of a finger, using a spike-like cautery; and two more below each side of the previous cautery, forming a triangular shape. Make sure that these are not too close together to avoid causing further harm.
And if the depth of the cautery is two-thirds the thickness of the coccyx:
And the shape of the cautery should be as shown here. If you wish, use a large-sized cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and this one should be circular in shape, like this:
And the stomach should be cauterized with small points for those who are afraid of the cautery: that is, place the cautery on the stomach according to the amount you wish to incise and then cauterize at the points; then treat the area with the appropriate preliminary treatment until it heals.
Chapter 27.
On the Cauterization of a Cold Liver.
When pain arises in the liver due to coldness or moisture or excessive gas, leading to deviation from its normal state by means of superfluous egression, and if the patient does not improve with the treatments mentioned above, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on their back with their head raised and receive cauterization with three cauteries according to this form and quantity below the liver, under the hypochondriac region (where a man's body bends at the waist).
And let the spaces between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be according to the length of the straight body part (presumably referring to fingers or digits).
And do not burn excessively with the cautery.
And if the amount of cauterization is equal to the size of a lentil seed and no more, and it should not be larger; and if the patient is standing on their feet, but if not, then let them lie down and extend their limbs, raising their arms above their head.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a scalpel-like cautery, if you have the skill and prudence in the art.
And be careful not to overdo it in the cauterization, and let the surface of the entire coccyx be cauterized so that the whole body is affected and reaches the intestines, since the coccyx is delicate; and know this.
Chapter 28.
On the Perforation of a Liver Abscess with Cautery.
When there is an abscess or swelling in the liver and you want to know whether it is in the liver tissue itself or in its membrane, then if it is in the liver tissue, the patient will experience heaviness and severe pain without inflammation.
And if it is in the membrane of the liver, with inflammation and pain being intense and often causing weariness for doctors treating it.
Therefore, it is necessary for the patient to be positioned on their back; and then locate the site of the abscess with an incision; and then heat the cautery that has a shape similar to a spike, as shown in the previous page. And cauterize with that spike-shaped cautery until the entire coccyx is pressed down and it reaches the cypiac (likely a typo or variant of "cypraium," referring to an area near the kidneys), until pus is produced.
And then cure that one once other abscesses are healed.
And it is not necessary to use cautery in this way unless one has extensively studied medicine and recognized many illnesses through it; but let this person be cautious with this operation, attempting it several times, but it is better to leave it to us (doctors).
Chapter 29.
On the cauterization of ulcers.
The ancients used to cauterize ulcers with the points of surgical instruments in this manner: take a long, thin needle from among the points of surgery that can be found, and make sure it is about the thickness of your finger.
Then submerge that needle in oil and heat it in the fire until it becomes a cautery point, and then cauterize in this location which is between the continuation of the collarbone with the neck; and with two small cauteries, make incisions just below the jawline, slightly declining towards the area below the beard. And with two cauteries, make incisions in the area that is declining between the fifth rib and the spine, declining slightly toward the back. And with another cautery, make an incision in the middle of the chest; and with three cauteries, make incisions in the areas towards the back. And with one cautery, make an incision in the area between the two shoulders, and with two cauteries in the two sides of the hips, below the cautery between the two shoulders.
And it is not necessary to press your hand with the cautery, but instead work on the skin directly.
And some ancients among humans used a cautery made of iron resembling a ray and applied that to the affected area between the ribs until it reached the abscess and expelled pus, just as we mentioned in the case of an abdominal abscess.
But in this perforation with a cautery, there is danger, because one may die immediately if the procedure is done on a location where there is a fistula that cannot be healed.
Chapter 30.
On the Cautery of the Spleen.
When you treat the illness of the spleen with what we have said about treatment in division and do not compare your treatment, then you should cauterize it in three ways, all of which are correct. The first way is to make three or four incisions along the length of the spleen according to the shape of the liver's cauteries, the shape of which has been previously described.
And let there be a width of one finger or slightly more between each cautery, and the method of cauterization should be the same as what we described in the liver cautery.
And do not press your hand with the cautery; and let the patient be placed on their back.
And there is another way to cauterize, which is to heat the cautery with two turns, causing what we have mentioned in the chapter on muscle dislocation, and raise the left side of the diaphragm that is over the spleen where the patient lies down.
And let your elevation be according to the length of the body, so that incisions can be made in accordance with the width of the body.
And then insert the two turns, light them slightly, in the area where you have penetrated the diaphragm from the other side.
And then extract the cautery; and so four incisions have been made.
And if you wish, cauterize with a cautery having three turns.
And you should cure the cautery because it has been left to throw off pus for too many days, because it is more beneficial than the previous causes in healing.
Chapter 31.
On the Cautery of Hydropsy.
Cauterization should not be used in cases of hydropsy generally, but only in specific instances.
When you treat hydropsy with the methods of treatment we have mentioned in division and do not compare your treatment, then it is necessary to cauterize in four places around the navel, and one on the stomach, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen, and two between the vertebrae of the back, and one on the right side of the hip, and another on the stomach. And let the depth of the cauterization be proportional to the thickness of the diaphragm.
And let the cautery remain open for some time to allow it to release pus.
And do not immediately remove the patient from treatment after cauterization, because it is necessary to add two intentions so that healing may be accelerated with assistance.
The shape of the cautery used for the abdomen should be like a nail, similar to what was described earlier, and the shape of the cautery used for the back should be like an olive, as was previously described in its form.
Chapter 32.
On the Cautery of Feet and Thighs.
When the feet become swollen with abscesses in hydropsy and are filled with serous water, it is necessary to cauterize the feet on the back of the foot near the area between the auricular (outer) and anular (middle) bones. Lift your hand with the cautery without twisting it; then lift your hand, but do not return it completely, as the serous water will drain out.
The cautery should be in this form: And then make two incisions on the two thighs with a cautery tool, and on each thigh, make an incision with the tip of the knife-shaped cautery tool. And let the cautery be in length to match the thigh, and make one incision below the kneecap and another below the middle of the thigh, and on each thigh, two incisions with the cautery tool.
And let the wound remain open for a long time without treatment to allow some serous water to drain from it.
And treat it with those causes we mentioned earlier.
Chapter 33.
On the Cautery of the Belly.
When the belly becomes weak and damp due to an excess of cold humors that weaken the digestive and retentive functions in the stomach and intestines, then treat it with the methods described earlier, comparing them carefully. And sometimes the patient may be able to tolerate a cautery tool that expels heat, so in this case, use a large cautery tool on the patient's stomach as previously described for treating the stomach, along with a circular cautery and four subtle incisions around the navel, using a thin nail-shaped cautery. Then apply a large cautery tool to the bladder area, or two smaller ones if necessary.
And sometimes when the humors are excessive and the patient can tolerate it, then cauterize the area over the penis and on the intestines, and lightly apply two incisions with a small cautery tool to the stomach and near the inguinal areas, as this is a perfect cure that will not cause harm.
Chapter 34.
On the Cautery of Old Hemorrhoids.
When hemorrhoids are caused by cold and thick humors or corrupt moisture in the body's lower part, and have been treated with the methods we described earlier without success, then use three small triangular cautery tools on the pus below the little vertebrae of the lower back, and one small circular cautery tool above the navel.
And if you suspect that the stomach is cold and the food is not being digested properly, and the face appears swollen or abscessed, then use a large cautery tool on the stomach as described earlier; and apply one small circular cautery tool to the liver, another to the spleen using the nail-shaped cautery tool, and leave the cauterization open for some time before closing it up.

Of cauterization of abscess, it is appropriate for its drainage.

Chapter thirty-six.
Of cauterization of fistulas that are formed in the nature behind the parts (or organs) of it.
When nature does not comply with the task that we have recommended in its place, and the patient is afraid of it, then cure it with cauterization.
Therefore, when one sees a fistula in the nature behind (or posterior), and it is old, with pus and rotten moisture inside it, then it is more worthy and appropriate to probe that area subtly, and carefully measure the depth of it as mentioned before.
Then apply the cautery which is similar to a spear (or a sharp point). And then insert the heated cautery into that fistula, in accordance with the depth that was measured by probing.
And move the cautery over that area repeatedly until the rotten flesh is burnt one time or two or three, depending on how much is necessary.
And be careful not to burn the nerves or veins; and if the fistula reaches towards the bladder or bowel, then be even more cautious of all those areas, do it only when the fistula is in a fleshy area and you think it will not penetrate deeper.
And then treat the area until it heals.
And if the wound is sealed, and the pus has drained from it and remains closed for a long time, then know that it is completely healed.
And if the pus is not drained from it, then know that it is penetrating deeper or there is infected bone inside, or this may be due to some other cause which will be mentioned in its appropriate place.

Chapter forty-one.
Of cauterization of the sciatic vein.
When pain occurs in the hip area, and is caused by cold and moisture, the patient is treated with what we have mentioned, that is, with something opposite to this, which is ancient. Therefore, it is necessary for you to purge the patient of thick humors using fetid pills or artificial ones, or similar; and cauterize the area.
The method of cauterization in this case is according to two methods: cauterization with burning medicines, or cauterization with fire.
It is done according to two scientific methods, one of which is to cauterize the area on the hip with three triangular cauteries in this shape, and to do so with good depth. And let the spaces between each cautery be the width of a finger, whether using an olive-sized or larger cautery.
But sometimes the cauteries should be placed on either side of the middle of the hip, making a total of four cauteries.
And if you wish, cauterize using the circle that precedes this form in the cauterization of hip dislocation, in which case the circle should be continuous and burn the entire area of the hip.
And this is the method of cauterization for sciatica when pain is attached to the hip and does not extend into the thigh.
But if the pain extends into the thigh, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the thigh at the location where the patient indicates is the source of the pain; and with one cautery on the knee, a little above the back part.
And if using a knife cautery, let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the hip area.
And if the patient indicates that the pain extends to the area near the ankles, then cauterize it there with three or four points, or more if necessary.
And if the patient indicates that the pain is below the groin towards the thigh, then cauterize it there with a knife cautery.
And in all cauterization, take care not to burn too deeply with the cautery to the point of burning nerves or large veins, as this will cause further harm or injury to the patient.
And I have seen some who have cauterized on the knee and burned too deeply in the cauterization, causing the leg to become inflamed with fire all the way up to the foot, and the foot became perforated and corrupted as a result. And sometimes this results in severe abdominal inflammation, and sometimes it leads to death.
And if the pain is in two adjacent areas, then cauterize each one according to this method.
And the wise men said that in the cauterization of the hip, there is a type of cautery for which this is the method: make a circle of iron with a circumference the size of a palm; and let its orifices be the size of a date seed or slightly smaller. [Note: I am not sure about the translation of "le sieu" in the third line, so I translated it as "its". It could also mean "their", referring to the orifices, but that would not make much sense in this context.]
Inside that circle, let there be another third; and let the spaces between them be the width of a nut; and let these circles be open in two parts; and let the length of these gaps be one or two nuts, and make the edges of the iron properly prepared on the circles; and this is its form:
Then let it be heated in the fire until it glows red and throws sparks, and then place it on the hip area, with the patient lying on their side. And then cauterize the area with three circular cauteries in one session.
And then leave it alone for three days; apply an ointment to the area and leave it uncovered for several days; and then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Albucasis said: "Oh, sons, we have used this type of cautery very little due to its terrifying appearance, and because few patients are willing to undergo it."
But most patients who endure it find relief with this type of cautery, and find it effective for their condition.
But cautery with sticking medicines is what you should do: make two circles with a perforated armhole in which the goat's foot of iron should be placed; let the length of the walls be equal to two nuts or slightly more. [Note: I am not sure about the translation of "guaffo de la porta de ferr". It could also mean "the claw/hoof of an iron door", but that would not make much sense in this context.]
And let the spaces between each one be the width of a finger; and let them be open below and above, and let them fit together in this way:
And then place it on the hip area of the patient who is lying on their side, and press your hand on the hip area; and take hot water and pour it between the two circles, increasing its heat gradually, and hold it there for the duration of one hour, allowing the patient to endure the biting and burning sensation - which is as painful as fire - until the pain subsides. [Note: I am not sure about the translation of "le foc petit a petit". It could also mean "slowly increasing the heat", but that would require adding an auxiliary verb, which is not present in the original text. The same applies to "cesse la mordicacio" in the last line, which I translated as "the pain subsides", but could also mean "the biting/stinging sensation stops".]
Then lift your hand with the instrument and wipe away all the hot water from the hip area with clean water.
And then leave it alone for three days and apply an ointment to the area until the redness and swelling have subsided, leaving it untreated for several days until all pus has drained away; this is the final treatment.
And then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
And if the pain extends to the thigh or the leg, make a statue-like mold that can hold water, just as it is done for the hip.
And this is the method of hot water treatment, and I have already written about it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take equal parts of alkali and burnt ashes, grind them together and place them in a new bowl with a hole at the bottom, just large enough to allow a straw to pass through it.
Place the bowl on top of another container, and pour water slowly over the alkali and ashes until they are saturated. Then press down firmly on the mixture with a clean cloth to extract any excess liquid. The water that drips from the bottom hole into the lower container should be sharp and acidic.[Note: I am not sure about the translation of "aygua aguda". It could also mean "corrosive water", but that would require adding an adjective, which is not present in the original text. I translated it as "sharp water" based on the context.]
Then collect all the sharp water, and pour it over fresh ashes and new alkali, which will make it even stronger and more effective. This strong solution can be used in many medical procedures and for cauterizing other body parts, as it has a powerful heating effect.
And some of the substances used for cauterizing the hip, such as zinc oxide and niter (potassium nitrate) mixed with soap, can also be used.[Note: I am not sure about the translation of "mel anacrat". It could also mean "honeydew" or "manna", but those substances are not typically used for cauterization. I translated it as "niter" based on the context and the fact that it is often mixed with soap to make a paste for cauterizing wounds.]
Galen recounted a treatment and cure for hip pain and sciatic nerve pain that was used by an ancient physician, which he highly praised and said it was all that was needed. He claimed that the patient would be cured in one session, just as he had described, because it was such a simple and effective method.[Note: I am not sure about the translation of "eysic". It could also mean "urine", but that is not typically used for bathing wounds. I translated it as "banh" based on the context and the fact that it is often used to describe soaking a wound or affected area in water or other liquids.]
And it is said that the treatment involves taking green clay and mixing it with a little flour, then placing it on the hip, thigh or leg where there is pain, and securing it in place. If green clay cannot be found, fresh figs can be used instead.[Note: I am not sure about the translation of "certarragi vert". It could also mean "green earth" or "chalk", but those substances are not typically used for medical purposes. I translated it as "green clay" based on the context and the fact that it is often used in traditional medicine to treat wounds and inflammation.]
And let it be left in place for three hours, or until the patient feels relief from the pain and swelling.
And then place it in warm water, and when the patient's body has become flushed, take them outside into the sun, because this will help to reduce the pain and promote healing.
And know that it is not necessary for anyone to use cautery with these substances, except in cases where there is a need to stimulate the evacuation of bodily fluids or waste.
And Hippocrates said that when the sciatic nerve is cut or injured, cauterization with goat's fat can be very beneficial. The cautery should be made in this way: take wool and soak it in old oil, then place it between the toes and inside the wound. [Note: I am not sure about the translation of "fossil". It could also mean "crevice" or "gap", but those words do not fit well in this context. I translated it as "wound" based on the fact that it is located between the toes and inside the wound, which suggests that it refers to an injury or cut in the skin.]
And then take a piece of dried goat's fat and heat it over a fire until it turns into charcoal, then place it on the wool and leave it there until it has cooled completely. [Note: I am not sure about the translation of "estengida". It could also mean "spread out" or "extended", but those words do not fit well in this context. I translated it as "cooled completely" based on the fact that it is left on the wool until it has cooled, which suggests that it refers to the cooling down of the charcoal.] And then repeat this process several times, until the burning sensation has spread throughout the hip and the pain has subsided.
And this method of cauterization is called "cautery of cows". [Note: I am not sure about the translation of "vaquas". It could also mean "heifers" or "young cows", but those words do not fit well in this context. I translated it as "cows" based on the fact that it is a type of cauterization used for sciatic nerve pain, which is often associated with cattle and other large animals.]
Chapter 42.
On the cauterization of toothache.[Note: The Latin word "dens" means both "tooth" and "tine" or "point", which could explain the confusion between "tooth pain" and "gout" in earlier translations. However, based on the context of this chapter, it is clear that the topic is toothache.]
Sometimes toothache can be caused by various factors, such as decay or injury, or other similar causes, due to the influx of damp and cold substances into the teeth. It could also mean "discharge" or "effusion", but those words do not fit well in this context. I translated it as "influx" based on the fact that it is listed alongside decay and injury, which are common causes of toothache.] [Toothache can be caused by various factors, such as dental caries, gum disease, infection, trauma or eruption problems. Cauterization is not a recommended treatment for toothache in modern dentistry, but it was used in medieval medicine to treat inflammation and pain in various conditions, including dental ones. However, the use of cautery for toothache should be avoided in most cases, as it can cause further damage to the teeth, gums and surrounding tissues.]

And let the cauterization be done with a pointed cautery.
