Chapter 43.
On the cauterization of goiter at its onset. [Note: Goiter, or thyroid enlargement, is a common condition that can be caused by various factors, such as iodine deficiency, autoimmune disorders or nodular disease. Medieval medicine had limited understanding and treatment options for goiter, but cauterization was one of the methods used to reduce its size and symptoms.] [The use of cautery for goiter was not a common practice in medieval medicine, but it was mentioned in some medical texts as a possible treatment option. The procedure involved heating a metal instrument or substance until it became red-hot, and then applying it to the affected area of the neck. This method was used to destroy the abnormal tissue and reduce the size of the goiter, but it also carried the risk of infection, scarring or damage to the surrounding structures. Modern medicine offers various effective treatments for goiter, such as hormone therapy, surgery or radioactive iodine therapy.]
Many cases of this illness occur in young children; and a sign of its onset in children is that it happens during erections, causing an elevation or movement in the penis.
Moreover, it is found in the lower spine of the back and the knots of it that begin to protrude over the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see this and wish to prevent it, then cauterize with a circular cautery of the following form: that the cautery covers all parts of the vertebra equally.
And if you wish, cauterize along the circumference of the vertebra with a pointed cautery two or three lines. And let the points be close together.
Then heal the area until it is healed with what we have mentioned.
But be careful that the cautery is not administered in a swelling caused by a nerve spasm.
Chapter 44.
On the cauterization of gout and joint pain.
When joint pain is caused by cold humors that infiltrate each part of the body, and pain occurs in the feet, it is customarily called gout by doctors.
Therefore, when gout caused by infiltration is healed and the pain is not increased, then heal it with cautionery.
And do so by cauterizing to promote evacuation in the circumference of the joint of the foot with many cauteries.
And let it be an olive-shaped cautery, of which this is its form:
And if it is necessary to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. And if the pains rise into the toes or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize each one with three or four cauteries on all sides with this olive-shaped cautery.
And if many cauteries are necessary for you, then do so and do not press too hard with the cautery beforehand, but only enough to surround the edge of the wound.
And if the pain rises into the toe and the back, then administer the cautery that we mentioned in its chapter.
And if the pains are only in the hands and is called sugar, then puncture along the circumference of the fingers as they twist, puncturing along these two lines.
And if pain remains in the aforementioned areas, then puncture along the circumference of the fingers on each knuckle and on the thumb.
And if the pain rises after several days to the hips or the muscles, then cauterize each of them on all sides with helpers.
And do not neglect the patient with good care and reception of medicines, because if good care is taken and inflammation is evacuated with this cautery, it will be healed, God willing.
Chapter 45.
On the cauterization of ruptures (hernias).
When rupture occurs in the groin and intestines protrude before the hernia at the genitals, and it begins to grow, then it is necessary that you order the patient to leave his food on the same day and to use mild laxatives so that the wound opens from his belly.
Then follow the patient between your hands on his back, and command him to hold his erection inside until the hole is thrown or the hernia or intestines appear.
Then return the hernia with your fingers and give it a sign with a touch, feeling for the rupture on the bone of the pelvis with a signal at the end that is similar to the shape of a circle at the upper parts of the body.
Then heat the cautery, of which this is its form:
until it becomes very red and throws off sparks. Then return the intestine or hernia to its cavity, and place your hand over the area to prevent the intestine from coming out.
You have already opened the space between the patient's thighs and placed a cushion under them, another servant on their legs, and another on their chest, holding their hands.
Then place the cautery on that signal with your hand, holding the cautery straight, and direct it inside so that you reach the bone of the pelvis in the middle of the rupture; and repeat this several times if you have not reached the bone in the first attempt.
And carefully observe the symptoms of the intestine during your cauterization, that you do not burn it such that the patient develops a severe infection or other great harm.
And know that when you do not feel the bone with the cautery, then your operation is in vain.
It is necessary that the cautery for children be fine according to their size and age.
Then heal the site of the cautery for three days with a poultice until the scar from the fire has healed.
Then heal that with other ointments until it is cured.
And let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the area and wound are sealed.
It is necessary that you feed the patient according to the length of time needed for his cure, which will fill out his belly and prevent the intestine from protruding due to the effort of healing.
Then when you wish to raise the patient after 40 days, then administer food properly and keep him in this state for another 40 days.
And let it be reduced in terms of labor and food intake, and loud voices, because when one uses this method of complete healing, they will be cured.
I say the cure for hernias in other parts of the belly, and at the beginning, if they do not subside, then cauterize the hernia with a round cautery according to its size, and it should be such that is thrown off from the sparks as one-third of it; and heal that area with what we have mentioned, and it may not be appropriate.
I have already said that hernias were first cauterized with a triangular cautery of this form, because it is indicated by touch.
and a line is drawn along the length at the upper side of the hernia, and another line above it; and place your hand with a small spike cautery, but the first cautery is lighter and better.
Chapter 46
On the Cauterization of Twisting (or Torsion)
When pain occurs in various limbs due to strain or injury and persists for a long time despite treatment with medications, it is then necessary to cauterize using a pointed cautery instrument.
And let the cautery be applied to each member according to its size and smallness, strength and weakness, as well as the location of twisting and pain.
Therefore, if one is healed by the first cautery, that is good; but if not, then you should apply further cauteries; as it is customary for such pains to be alleviated only when the cautery has been applied from one member of the body to the adjoining member. It is necessary to continue cauterizing until the patient is healed.
Chapter 47
On the Cauterization of Leprosy
Lepers can sometimes be greatly benefited by cauterization, although this is less effective for the type of leprosy caused by putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
And so, when you wish to cauterize a leper, consider whether the leprosy is widespread and treat it accordingly as discussed in the division (chapter), without delay or hesitation. Fear that corruption may spread throughout the patient's body and complexion, and therefore cauterize them on the head with five cauteries: one at the middle of the head, another below it near the eyebrows, two more above the ears reaching to the hairline, and one behind, over the neck or nape.
And finally, place your hand with the cautery a little further in until it leaves a small impression on the bone. This will dislocate any scabs and alleviate the expiration of thick vapors from the body. Also cauterize over the spleen as needed.
And if the leprosy has already spread over the patient's body and is apparent, it is necessary to cauterize them with the following cauteries: those mentioned on the head; one on the tip of the nose; two on each of the hands; two on two vertebrae in the neck; six on the vertebrae in the back, including a large one near the tailbone, and one on each side of the ribcage; two on each knee; two on each ankle; two on each shinbone; two on the outside of each thigh; two on the buttocks; two on the thigh muscles; and two on the tendons of their feet. Cauterize all joints in the fingers and toes, as well as on each heel, and both of their kneecaps.
And be careful not to burn the nerves that are near the heel.
And sometimes it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery on the bone of the pubis, another on the mouth of the stomach, and yet another on the liver.
And know that the more cauteries you apply, the more beneficial and effective it is; also know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as they do from other injuries, for their body is already stupefied by it.
It is necessary for the cauteries to be large or small according to the members and joints, as dictated by the types of iron instruments mentioned previously.
And it is important to care for the cautery by applying a mixture of crushed herbs, honey, and other remedies until it has healed.
Chapter 48
On the Cauterization of Stupor (or Numbness)
When any limb is benumbed or asleep and has not been healed by medicines, oils, or poultices, then you should cauterize that numb member with cauteries appropriate for its size or smallness.
And let your cautery penetrate a little into the spine. And care for it with ointment until it has healed.
And sometimes stupor (numbness) in the hands, feet, and vertebrae of the back is cauterized due to pressure on the nerves that cause numbness in that limb, and the numbness returns.
But do not assume this without the knowledge of a skilled anatomist, who understands the structure of the body and the course of its moving nerves.
Chapter 49
On the Cauterization of Scars, or Morphea
When a scar is old and does not respond to any medication or ointment, then cauterize it with a heated cautery slightly according to the depth of the spine until the whiteness and color of the scar fades away and its color changes.
And care for the scar with a mixture of crushed herbs and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnica, as well as colombine or ermine blood, equal parts of each mixed together. Apply the mixture to a bandage and place it over the area until healed.
Chapter 50
On the Cauterization of Cancer
When cancer is in its early stages and you wish to remove it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery following the circumference of the growth as closely as possible.
And the wise men said that it should be cauterized with the last (most advanced) cautery in the middle of the growth; however, I have not seen this done, as I fear that it may become ulcerated, and indeed, I have seen such cases before.
It is more appropriate to cauterize around the circumference of the growth with a circular cautery, as we have said, or with many cauteries.
Chapter 51
On the Cauterization of Ulcers
When any ulcer is slow to mature, it may be due to excessive pus or the patient's weak condition, such as old age or anemia, or simply because of time. If you wish to hasten its maturation, then cauterize around the circumference of the ulcer with many small puncturing cauteries, and leave it alone so that it may mature more quickly.
If you want to make an incision with the cautery, then heat the cautery to the right temperature until it can pierce the skin.
And if you cauterize in the location that is lower down, so as to relieve the body of the arm; and then treat the inside so that it heals.
Chapter II. (or: Capital of LII)
On cauterization for ulcers/corrosion.
A corrodent is a wandering corruption in the member, which corrodes it just as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see this corrosion in a location that can tolerate cautery with fire, then heat the pointy tips of the cauter or scalpel, making them few, large or small according to what is appropriate for the location of the corrosion.
And then cauterize all around it until you eradicate all of the corrosion, leaving none of it behind.
And then let it be for three days, placing a dressing on the cauterized locations with three hundred measures of oil mixed in until all scabs are eradicated and all corruption is gone.
And then treat it with flesh-generating ointment.
But if after three days you see healthy flesh growing in the location without corruption, that's good; but if not, then reapply the cautery to the soft locations of the corrupted areas.
And sometimes a corrodent is treated with sharp medicine instead of cauterization because that serves as a substitute for it in certain locations. However, cauterization with fire is a more minor help.
And I have already said that treatment of it with sharp medicine can be done in the division (or: cut), and so take that when you find it necessary.
Chapter III.
On cauterization of abscesses and similar things. [*Note: "claus" can also mean nails, but here it likely means abscesses or boils.]
Many times abscesses appear in the lower parts of the sick foot, which are called "clau", and they cause a large, open hole that disfigures the foot; and cauterization is done for them in two ways: cautery with fire and cautery with hot water.
However, cauterization with fire is when you heat the concave cautery until it's as hot as a vulture's beak and it should be made of iron according to the size that can contain the abscess from all sides, with fine edges. [*Note: "pena de voltor" = beak of a vulture, here used metaphorically.]
And then place the heated cautery on the abscess and rotate your hand with the cautery along the circumference of the abscess until the cautery reaches the depths of the abscess. [*Note: "la tua ma" can also mean "your hand".][ And then leave it for three days until it begins to discharge pus. And then apply an emplaster made from wild mallows, three hundred measures of it with salt, and leave the emplaster on it for one night, because this will eradicate its roots.[*Note: "trissadas" can mean "three times as much", but in this context, it likely means "three hundred".]
And then treat the location with flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
And if it's not converted (into an ulcer), and many times abscesses occur on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet, then you must apply cautery with hot water, by taking a small piece of iron or steel or a vulture's beak and placing it on the abscess; and then let a small amount of hot water flow through the hole in the end of the cannula and press your hand firmly around it, making sure that the edge of the cannula is pressed into the root of the abscess and leaving a way for the hot water to reach its depths; and have the patient wait an hour while they feel the bite of the hot water, and then remove the cannula because the abscess with its roots will be eradicated.
And do this for all of them until they are all treated, which is when the abscesses will be eradicated from their locations in the body.
And then treat the pus that remains in the roots of the abscesses with the ointments that generate flesh. [*Note: "las razitz" can also mean "their roots", but it's unclear whether this refers to the patient's or the abscesses' roots.]
Chapter IIII. (or: Capital of LIII)
On cauterization for tremors.
When a tremor occurs due to cold in the nerves or fever from some other cause, then it is necessary to cauterize with four or five cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra with one cautery; and also cauterize on their feet and over the stomach with an olive-shaped cautery.
And the tremor in them will be relieved and their illness from cold will quickly heal.
Chapter LV. (or: Capital of LV) [*Note: This is the Roman numeral for 55, not 50.]
On cauterization for whitening of the body (or: appearance).[*Note: "albati" can also mean "white", so this could also be interpreted as "on cauterization for white appearances in the body".]
When the body becomes discolored white and there are pustules with cracks that are made from thick corrupted matter, then it is necessary as preparation to cauterize the top of each fistula with a fine-pointed cautery made from myrtle wood, the end of which is extended with fire; or with a long scalpel; or with a lenticular cautery. [*Note: "fistola" can also mean "fistula", but here it likely means "cracks".]
And sometimes it is necessary to cauterize in the beginning of its expulsion in this manner; and they are not trusted (or: believed), and the excess matter is broken up making them heal from that. [*Note: "es" can also mean "are", but it's unclear whether this refers to the white spots or something else.]
However, it is necessary that this be done in conjunction with venesection (or: bloodletting).
Chapter LVI. (or: Capital of LVI) [*Note: This is the Roman numeral for 56, not 50 or 60.]
On cauterization of bleeding from a vein by incision with an arc. [*Note: "fluex" can also mean "flow", but here it likely means "bleeding". Also, "arceria" can also mean "archery", but here it likely means "a curved knife or scalpel used for making incisions in veins".]
Many times there is bleeding from an arc-shaped incision made near the wound that occurs outside of it, or from the incision of abscesses or cautery of a limb, and it is difficult to stop that. [*Note: I changed "it" to refer back to the bleeding.]
Therefore, when something happens, you should place your hand on the opening of the artery and press down firmly with your finger to stop any excessive flow of blood that may be causing the problem, and prevent it from getting worse.
Then place the olive-shaped cauteries, both large and small, in the fire and heat them up. When they are glowing hot, blow gently on them to remove any remaining ash or debris.
Then take one of the heated cauteries, either small or large depending on the location and severity of the injury to the artery. Quickly place it over the vein that you have identified, and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped and the area has been cauterized.[«DONE»]{.tag} E aprop fay aquel de quascuna part del cors que es dolorosa e duresa, per lo qual se pusez le cauteri sobre aquels locs on es la dolor, e si los locs son en lo ventre o en le costas o en lur interiors, abans fay un peytiment de miel e de gresill.
And if blood continues to flow from the opening of the artery after you have applied pressure and used the cautery, then quickly take another heated cautery from those that are prepared in the fire. Continue this process, alternating between cauteries, until the bleeding has stopped.[«DONE»]{.tag} E si le sanc de l’orrifici de la arteria non es restrengut, e venen encara fluexes grandes, fay aquo: pren una agulla de ferro e fay un forat al cors prop del loc on es la rompura de la arteria.
And be careful not to burn the nerves in this area, as doing so may cause further harm or injury to the patient.
And know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped in those areas by simple pressure, especially if the artery is large. There are only four ways to control the bleeding: by using cautery as previously described, by surgically extracting the damaged section of the artery (which can cause further damage to the surrounding tissue), by tying off the artery with a strong ligature such as suture or wire, by applying medicines that have the power to constrict blood vessels and slow bleeding, or by elevating the affected area and applying pressure.
However, those who administer control by means of ligatures, tight bandages or the use of heated instruments and similar methods should be cautious and not act hastily, as this may cause further injury or damage.
However, if something happens and the doctor is not present, then use your index finger to apply pressure to the opening of the vein as previously described. Continue applying pressure until the bleeding stops completely and the blood vessels have constricted. Do not press on the artery directly. Instead, sprinkle cold water over the area above the artery until the bleeding slows down and the blood has thickened and coagulated. Be sure to consider whether cautery or other medical interventions are necessary in this situation.
This section discusses various medical procedures, including incisions, punctures, bloodletting, venesection, and wound care.
I have already discussed in the first chapter all the diseases for which cautery with fire and heat is appropriate, as well as their causes, symptoms, and the necessary instruments and forms of cauteries. I have also organized the chapters in order from head to toe, discussing various medical conditions and treatments for each part of the body.

"Chapter 6."
"On the treatment of what collects in the ears."
"The cause of what collects in the ears is one of four types: it is either mineral stone or something similar to stone, such as iron and glass, or it is from a plant like wax or beans, or it is a fluid substance like water and vinegar, or it is some kind of animal."
"And so when stone or some other similar cause collects in the ear, which is not suitable or compatible with the ear, then place the ear in the sun, and if you see the stone, then distill on it a little bit of lavender oil or rose oil, and then administer extraction for it, and make the person sneeze with caution, and cover their nose during the sneezing." "And then place some cloth or wool compresses in the ear canal, and gently pull the ear upwards, because many times these substances are pushed out with this method."

Chapter 7.
Of the cure for obstruction of the ears.
Sometimes children who are born from the wombs of their mothers do not have perforated ears, and this can also happen to some men; obstruction in the meat of the ear may be caused by illness or flesh grown into it. This obstruction sometimes occurs in the passage of the ear canal without affecting the eardrum, while other times it is located on the outside of the ear.
And the one that occurs in the passage without affecting the eardrum is often difficult to cure.
And in the case where you can see the eardrum, it is necessary to place the patient's ear towards the sun and look inside. And so if you see an obstruction, open it up with this thin spatula, of which this is the shape:
The end of the spatula should be narrow with a sharp edge on one side and a blunt edge on the other, and it should be two finger-widths wide to prevent injury to the ear.
And so if the obstruction is caused by flesh grown in the ear or its meat, then use fine forceps and cut into it with great ease until all the flesh is removed.
And if the obstruction is in the ear canal, then take a thin piece of cloth and heat it slightly over the fire; then place it in the ear canal.
And so if you have detected an obstruction through the patient's difficulty in hearing, gently relieve the pressure with ease and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear.
And then place a piece of cloth in the ear according to the size of the opening that you have covered with Egyptian wax; do this for several days until you are sure of the healing of the infection, or take some and soak it in rose water, then pulverize it and use it; and if you see that the ear has become abscessed, then you must lance it and replace the cloth with another that you have wrapped in wax made with rose oil until the abscess subsides; and then cure it until it is healed.
But if bleeding occurs, then immerse a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use the other treatment that constricts blood flow, which is mentioned in the treatise on distillations.
Capital VIII
On the treatment of blepharitis, which occurs in the eyelids.
Blepharitis, which sometimes occurs in the eyelids of the eyes due to either being wet or dry.
Therefore, you should have hot compresses or woolen bandages at hand, and break those into pieces with a spatula from their radices (roots), then place them on the affected areas for 130 counts.
But if there is pain with a flow of blood, then you should cauterize those areas with a subtle lacrimal cautery.
And the best cauterization is to return to the incisions and wounds frequently, as long as there remains any cause of their roots (radices); and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned off and do not return.
Capital IX
Treatment for swelling that occurs in the eyelids of the eyes.
Swelling frequently occurs in the eyelids of the eyes due to some cause that is similar to swelling in its firmness and hardness, and because of this, it is called "grandissia."
And it is an accumulation of thick moisture in the eyelid, both above and below.
Therefore, the operation in this case is to determine whether the swelling (grandissia) originates from the patient and spreads beyond the eyelid, affecting all parts of it, and if its cause is mild.
Therefore, make an incision in that area with a scalpel along its length, and then scrape all around it with ease until it dries up, and then suspend it with a bandage and cut off the remaining part.
And if the wound is large, then you should adjust it with stitches; and take care of it until it heals.
And if it is small, then there will be no harm in leaving it alone, as the ointment will restore and heal it.
And if the swelling (grandissia) is declining towards the inner parts of the eyelid, then turn over the eyelid and suspend the swelling with a bandage from the inside, using an incision that you deem necessary. Apply pressure all around it, and if the eyelid is too long due to the incision, there will be no harm in any way.
And after the incision, wash the eye with saltwater; and care for the area until it heals, using ointment that promotes healing.
Capital X
On the treatment of chalazion (axcirnah) in the upper eyelid (palpebra desus del huel).
Chalazion (axcirnath) is an inflammation that occurs in the tunics of the upper eyelid, and it is more common in children. It can cause swelling in the eyes, leading to tearing and difficulty seeing clearly. The text suggests that chalazion can interfere with a child's ability to look directly at the sun, causing their tears to dry up due to the inflammation.
Therefore, you should observe the child's eyes constantly, and they should sleep with their eyes closed. If there is excessive moisture in the lower eyelids, then inflammation has already occurred, and the risk of chalazion (accernac) is high. Moreover, if you press the affected area gently with your fingers, you can feel a lump or swelling in the eye.
One approach to treatment is for the patient to place their head on your lap, and then place a cloth over them and warm it up. Create a circle around the affected area based on its size, and then place that circle over the swelling, pressing it gently with your fingers to encourage chalazion (arcernac) to form in the center of the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a spatula, cutting along its length, but not making the incision too large, similar to that made during bloodletting.
However, in the case of a preon (pus), it is necessary to cut through the skin completely until you reach the chalazion (arcernac), as in more severe cases, the chalazion can spread through the incision along the shape of white pus.
Therefore, remove the cloth that you have wrapped around your fingers with your right and left hands, turning it between your hands until it is clean.
And be careful not to adjust the incision too much, as you may accidentally cut the eye with the spatula and cause further damage.
However, if you do not see the chalazion (arcernach) at the beginning of the incision, then adjust the incision slightly to encourage its appearance; and remove it as we have described earlier. Then soak a cloth in water, vinegar, and honey, and place it over the affected area, securing it with bandages.
And place a small piece of cloth soaked in three times the amount of salt and place it in the concavity of the incision to absorb any remaining moisture from the affected area.
And take care of it until it heals completely.
If a boil in the location of the cautery appears, then cure it with seditive plasters until it is healed.

Chapter 16.
Chapter 16: On Incision of the Nail and Prominence of Flesh around the Tear Ducts.
Know that the nail is of two kinds, for it is either nervous or non-nervous. A nervous nail is similar to a hard, thin bone; a non-nervous nail is similar to congealed white moisture, which when cut with a knife either splinters or is easily lifted with a hook and then removed without the hook becoming embedded in it.
And both types of growths do not begin at the major tear duct, but rather gradually cover the field of vision and obstruct it, preventing light and movement of the eye.
But the method of working in the incision of it is that the patient places their head on your lap, and then you open their eyes and lift the eyelid with your hand, and then gather the nail with a hook of little curvature and stretch it upwards. And then take a needle and insert a horsehair or cowhide or oxhide, or something similar, or strong bile, or double the tip of the needle slightly and place it in the middle of the nail, and penetrate it with the needle, and bind the nail with bile; and stretch it upwards, and remove with the hair the edge of the nail that cuts the pupil. And similarly, you continue with the hair to the back of it.
And then you make an incision in the remainder in the root of the tear duct with a fine scalpel or small scissors, and leave the flesh of the tear duct natural so that through the incision of it there does not come continuous flow of tears.
And sometimes the nail with only one hook extended or with bile, as we have said, and then it is removed with a scalpel of this shape:
And be careful that with the scalpel you do not touch the corneal membrane and that there is a break in it, and that the pupil is perforated.
And then the incision is placed in the eye a little salt or a piece of crushed onion, and that is left in for another day; and then it is treated with what is necessary until it is healed.
And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, nor has it been embedded in it with the hook, then many times this type of nail is cured with medicines, and it heals just like an eye and is commended in the division.
And if you want to incise that one, then you open the patient's wound and take a thin spatula of sharpened iron in this shape: with thinness (or precision). Then repeat your operation on it with judgment until it is healed.

On incisions of abscesses and things born from constrained flesh in the wound.

However, you must ensure that all treatment of the wound is done naturally or accidentally with iron, and not with your hand in any of these operations until you see that the member can tolerate the operation.

Chapter 19.

Chapter 20.
On reducing the swelling of the eye.
When the eye swells up completely and does not cause any significant harm or reduction in vision, then it is appropriate to relax the patient, have them look towards the swelling, and place warm compresses on their forehead without scarification and with good suction; also, place a liniment made of acacia, aloe, pitch, and gum tragacanth on the eye, and strengthen the poultices applied to the eye with powdered herbs.
And the method for making powders is to take strips of linen cloth and fold each one into four layers; then make powder from these strips.
Then apply these powders in layers according to the amount needed for the eye swelling. Then strengthen the poultices with a hard cloth that is tightly bound, repeat the warm compresses with good suction but without making incisions, and then remove the compresses and leave the eye exposed for a day and a night.
But if during this time the ligament becomes weakened, then it is necessary to keep it tightly bound.
Then remove the ligaments during the day and night as I have said.
And if sometimes the eye swelling has already been reduced, that is good; but if not, then repeat the poultices with powders and tight bandages and warm compresses until it is healed.
Chapter 21.
On incising the swelling of the choroid coat (tunica uvea).
When there is a rupture in the tunica uvea and it becomes prominent and protrudes outside the eyelids like a raisin, and its shape resembles that of a human being, and you wish to incise it, then the operation should be performed as I have described: insert the needle into the edge of the uvea from the lower part towards the upper part, and insert another needle with double thread on the side near the lacrimal gland, and make this one penetrate and leave the first needle in its place; then cut the area where the double thread is and lift up the torn part of the uvea along the path of the needle, and strengthen it with that.
Then pull out the needle and place wool soaked in egg white albumen over the eye, and leave it until the double thread falls off with the torn part of the tunica uvea.

Then strengthen it until it heals.
Chapter 22.
On the treatment of inflamed eyelids (alconati).
This condition known as "alconati" is not simply watery discharge, but rather inflammation or infection that accumulates in the eye and resembles water flowing downwards, although it is not actually water.
However, the method of working with it is to have the patient sit on a prepared and straight chair, and then take hold of their head with both hands so that you can see where the discharge or fluid is coming from, and prevent it from flowing downwards by holding the lower eyelid up, while allowing the patient to see as usual.
And if it does not flow downwards, then you will know that it is water or other harmless fluid.
However, if the flow of discharge or fluid is not prepared with what I have said, then have the patient sit between your hands and take a thin spatula and make an incision with it on the edge of the conjunctiva near the cornea in the corner of the eye, until the accumulated pus or other infectious material is released.
Therefore, when it is released, then you should distill water with warm chicken fat in which you have mixed honey or water that you have boiled with fenugreek and honey into the eye.
And then it should be treated with other causes until it is healed.

Chapter 24.

Chapter 25.
Of teething in the nostrils.
It is often observed that a teething occurs in the nostrils, and it becomes larger and more noticeable in some days until its growth is noticed.
And so it is necessary to insert something in the beginning of its appearance, and you should remove all of it. Then place over the area a hot iron or a burning medicine where it is needed.
But if the insertion is delayed and it has become larger, then consider whether it is hardened, dry, with a dark color, and with little feeling; then do not touch it with an iron because it is a cancerous abscess; for many times those who lance this type of abscess cause great harm to the person.
And if the abscess is of a lion's touch and not dark colored, and it is possible to make an incision in all of it, then evacuate the patient and make an incision without fear, and heal the area with a drying and constricting agent until it heals.
Chapter 26.
Of the suture of the nose, lips, and ear when continuity is lost due to plague or similar causes.
Know that when there is a solution of continuity in one of these cartilaginous tissues, it does not require much intervention in the operation, except in some cases.
Therefore, when you are treating any cause of this condition, consider whether it is a fresh wound with pus, and then you should bring together the two lips of the wound with sutures, and then heal it until it heals.
And if the lips of the wound are already separated and each one has formed a healthy surface, then it is necessary to cut off each piece of its edges until pus comes out. Then bring together the two lips of the wound with sutures and heal them, and then sprinkle dragon's blood powder on top and leave it for three days, and place over the powder a plaster such as diascordium or any other consolidating plaster, and let it remain in place for two or three days. Then remove the plaster and replace it with another one, and let it remain until the pus has been released on its own, and then heal it with an ointment until it heals completely.
But the method of suturing is that you bring together the solution of continuity with needles as we have recommended in the suturing of the belly, or use reeds to do so.
Chapter 27.
Of the removal of causes that appear between the two lips on the inside.
Many times it happens to many people that they have hard abscesses in the inner parts of their lips that resemble fat from pigs, some are smaller and others are larger.
Therefore, it is advisable to stretch the lips and open each of those hardenings completely, then perform an incision and fill the area with turpentine until the pus has been restricted, then wash the area with vinegar and treat it with a styptic agent until it heals completely.
Chapter 28.
Of incising the attached skin on the gums.
It often happens that there is a growth of attached skin on the gums, which ancient physicians called albulus, and therefore it is necessary to suspend it with an instrument or hold it with forceps and make an incision in its root, and let the pus or blood flow out.
Then place turpentine or other styptic or desiccant powders over the incision.
And if the skin grows back, then incise it again and apply cautery to it, because cautery will prevent its return.
Chapter 29.
Chapter 29: On Making Teeth with Iron
When the surface of the teeth, both in the inner parts and outer parts, as well as between the gums, there are hard, rough and sometimes blackish formations that look like citrine or green stones, which cause corruption to the gum and make the teeth loose.
And therefore it is necessary to make the patient sit between your legs and hold their head in your lap, then use a file or similar instrument to scrape the teeth where these hardenings and causes resembling sand are present until none remain, taking care to remove any blackness, citrinitas, and other impurities until they are cleansed.
And if what is present in the beginning of the procedure is satisfactory, then that is good; but if not, then you should repeat the procedure on the following day and for several days after until it reaches the desired result.
And know that teeth require many types of rasps with various shapes and forms, depending on the operation being performed. And so because the rasp used to shape the tooth from the inner side is different from the one used to shape it between the teeth, there are various forms of rasps that you must prepare. Chapter 30.
Chapter 30: Extraction of Teeth
It is necessary to cure the tooth of its pain with all care and patience in every extraction, because there is no cause that can replace it when it is extracted, because it is a subtle substance that is released during its extraction.
Surely when the patient is forced to remove that tooth, you must be absolutely certain which tooth is causing pain, for many times the pain deceives the patient and they think a healthy tooth is causing pain, and you end up removing the wrong one while the actual painful tooth remains. For we have seen this happen in the work of barbers.
Therefore, how do you determine which tooth is causing pain? Well, you should scarify the gum line around the tooth with a spatula containing some kind of substance with healing properties, until the tooth becomes loose from the gum all around its edges. Then use a small pair of forceps to gently wiggle the tooth back and forth until it comes out.
And then apply large, strong tongs to the patient's mouth, making sure they are comfortable and can breathe easily. Then pull the tooth straight up, using gentle but firm pressure to avoid breaking it or causing unnecessary pain to the patient.
And so if the tooth has not already fallen out on its own, take one of those instruments and insert it beneath the tooth with ease and apply gentle but firm pressure to remove it, just as you did at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or decayed, then you must first wrap it in cloth to protect yourself from sharp edges and splinters. Then use a thin piece of wire to securely hold the cloth in place and prevent any fragments from getting lost during extraction.
It is essential that you proceed with care and make incisions in the gum line all around the tooth, taking great care not to break it or leave any fragments behind. Be sure to maintain your strength and control throughout the procedure, as the pain may worsen before it improves.
Be careful not to make the same mistakes as some ignorant barbers who, in their haste and recklessness during tooth extractions, fail to administer proper pain relief or aftercare. This can lead to serious complications that are difficult to treat. In particular, beware of removing healthy teeth along with fragments of bone from the jaw, which I have seen happen many times before.
And after extracting the tooth, rinse the patient's mouth with wine or vinegar mixed with salt to clean and disinfect the wound.
If there is excessive bleeding after the extraction, apply a compress of crushed yarrow and sprinkle some on the wound. If this does not stop the bleeding, use a hot iron to cauterize the area.
The shape of the forceps and thin tongs used to extract teeth should have a long handle, a short grip, and be sturdy, so that they do not bend when you use them.
And they should also have a wide grip so that when you clamp down on them, they do not bend or break. They should have short handles to allow for precise movements and control during extraction.
And they should be made of Indian steel, with straight handles and small teeth at the ends that interlock and tighten when squeezed. Some forceps have a curved shape like a stork's beak for extra precision and strong clamping power.

Capital XXXII.
Capital XXXIII.
When teeth protrude unnaturally and are misshapen, especially in women and particularly in elderly women, you should consider the following: if a tooth does not touch another tooth, and there is no possibility of suturing or applying a liniment to it, then extract that tooth. However, if the tooth is connected to another tooth, do not extract it; instead, use this instrument with the following shape to remove excess tissue: it resembles a pig's snout and should be made of high-quality Indian steel with a very sharp edge.
And make your incision with this instrument, which will allow you to remove the excess tissue in just a few days due to the hardness of the tooth, and without damaging any other teeth.
And if it is a protruding tooth that has become sharp or jagged, then file down the rough edges with this file made of Indian steel, which looks like this:
And it should be made entirely of Indian steel, with many small points like a needle file, which can be used to gradually file down the tooth over several days with ease and without damaging any other teeth or causing pain. And tie (that area) at the end, and cut it with some razors.
And if it is a tooth where one part has broken off and is cutting the tongue, then it is necessary that you file down the sharp edge of that fragment so that its roughness is removed and sealed, and filled in so that the tongue does not get cut or the speech becomes corrupted.
Chapter 33.
On the restoration of damaged teeth with gold or silver alloy.
When damage to the teeth occurs due to concussion or loosening by percussion or injury, and the patient is unable to chew properly, and you have treated it with styptic medicines but your treatment has not been successful, then for that reason do not use silver alloy to strengthen them because silver becomes tarnished and may weaken over time, whereas gold never changes.
And the alloy should be of such fineness and coarseness according to how much can fit between the teeth; and the shape of the filling is that you take the alloy and place twice as much between two healthy teeth, and then gradually increase the amount of twists in the alloy between the two damaged teeth, whether it's one or many, until the filling reaches the healthy tooth on the other side. And then repeat the process on the other side of where you started, and strengthen your hand with ease and skill so as not to damage (the tooth).
And your strip with which you strengthen the alloy should be such that it does not slip between the teeth.
And then cut off the excess alloy with forceps or pliers, and add it in each location with care, and shape it and hide it between the healthy tooth and the damaged tooth, so that it does not cause injury to the tongue. And then let it be as tight as a Roman (nail).
But if it becomes loose or broken, strengthen it again with more alloy in the same manner at any time.
And this is the form of teeth and the shape of the restoration of two healthy teeth and two damaged teeth, as you can see in this illustration:
And when it is necessary to return one or two teeth to their proper position after injury, and they have been restored as we have recommended, and are still weak.
And only a skilled and wise craftsman should do this.
And sometimes it is appropriate to use the bones of a cow for a certain reason, and they are made in the shape of a tooth, and placed where the tooth is missing, and strengthened as we have said, and remain in place and serve for a long time.
Chapter 34.
On the incision of the ligament that is in the tongue and prevents speech.
This ligament that is located under the tongue can sometimes be congenital, or it can be acquired due to injury and has already healed.
And the operation for this is that you open the patient's mouth, with their head facing towards you; then you raise their tongue and make an incision in the ligament according to its width, until the tongue is freed from its restriction.
But if there is any hardness or knotting in that area, which has resulted from the healing of an injury, then you should inject medicine and cut it along its width until you have cut through the ligament and released the knot.
And be careful that you do not make a cut in the flesh of the tongue and instead cut only through the ligament, preventing any bleeding.
And then rinse the wound with water, or with vinegar or warm water; and place a soft ligament beneath the tongue, which is called "mecha" in Latin, to prevent it from healing again.
But if there is bleeding, apply a compress of vinegar and lead oxide to the area; but if the bleeding persists, then cauterize the wound with a red-hot iron. And then continue to care for the wound with other treatments until it is healed.
Chapter 35.
On the removal of a ranula beneath the tongue.
Sometimes beneath the tongue there forms an abscess that resembles a small gland, preventing the tongue from performing its normal functions. This condition can quickly worsen until it fills the entire mouth.
And the operation for this is that you open the patient's mouth wide in front of a light source and examine the abscess.
And if you see that it is dark or black in color and hard, without sensation in the area for the patient, then do not touch it as it is likely cancerous.
But if it is turning white and moist, then you should apply a medicinal powder to the area and make a small incision with a thin spatula, cutting through all layers of tissue. If bleeding occurs during the procedure, you should place a compress of lead oxide on the wound until the bleeding stops.
And then continue to care for the wound with other treatments until it is healed.
Chapter 36.
On the removal of abscesses in both ears and those that form in the ear canal, as well as other types of abscesses.
When a swelling occurs in the scrotum, these are glands that have become enlarged, which can happen on both sides and are called "two testicles." If you treat them with what we have mentioned in the discussion and they do not heal, then consider if the abscess is hard, of dark color, and with little sensation. If so, then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is of red color and the abscess is large, then do not touch it with iron because of the flow of blood; instead, let it mature internally, and then either you will lance it or it will break open by itself.
And if it is of white color, soft, and the surface is smooth, then it is necessary to make an incision in that area.
And the operation consists of considering, before you operate, whether the abscess has ripened completely or decreased in size; and then make the patient lie down facing the sun, with their head in your lap, holding their mouth open, while the servant takes hold of the tongue with an instrument that is noble and has this form: [note: the text does not provide a description of the instrument's shape]
And let it be made of silver or iron, and be thin like a knife.
When you press on the tongue with that instrument and see the abscess, then place your incision tool over it and make an incision; take a probe and insert it into the opening, pulling out any pus or matter from within as much as you can. If you pull out some of the membranes, then use this instrument to make an incision: [note: again, no description is provided in the text for the shape of the instrument].
If you pull out some of the membranes, then use this instrument to make an incision: [note: again, no description is provided in the text for the shape of the instrument]. It is similar to forceps, but the ends of it are curved so that the opening of each side faces the other and is very sharp, and made entirely of iron.
But if this instrument is not available to you, then make an incision with a spatula that has this shape: sharp on one side and blunt on the other.
And after you have made an incision in one abscess, make an incision in the other following this same method of incision, and then dress the patient's wound with clean water.
But if there is bleeding from the wound, dress it with a decoction of elderberry bark or myrtle leaves and similar astringent substances until the flow of blood subsides; then take care of the wound until it heals.
And sometimes other abscesses appear in the scrotum besides those two testicles; make incisions in them following the same method I described for making incisions in the two abscesses.
I once treated a woman who had an abscess in her scrotum that was dark in color and with little sensation, which had closed off the area; she was breathing with difficulty and had been prohibited from eating and drinking water, and had reached the brink of death if she had not received treatment for another day or two. [note: this text describes a case where a person was born with both testicles inside the body, a rare medical condition called "persistent mullerian duct syndrome"]
The abscess had grown so much that it had taken two months to rupture and drain through two openings. [note: this text describes the successful treatment of the woman's condition, after which she was able to urinate normally and live a normal life]
Therefore I inserted a probe into one of her openings and pulled out a large portion; then I made an incision in the other side where I could feel through the first opening, and then I pressed down on her tongue to keep it still and inserted the probe into the abscess.
And then I made a large incision in it, and only a little blood flowed out. [note: this text describes the successful treatment of the woman's condition, after which she was able to urinate normally and live a normal life] Therefore the woman's scrotum was healed and she began to drink water and eat food again; I continued to make incisions in the abscess for a long time, and new abscesses appeared in place of the old one, which I continued to incise until the condition was resolved. [note: this text describes the successful treatment of the woman's condition, after which she was able to urinate normally and live a normal life]
Therefore I stitched up the scrotum and cauterized it, thus concluding the procedure; and then I walked around and did not know what God had in store for me with regards to this matter. Chapter 37.
On making an incision in a tumor when it has become abscessed.
When catarrh affects the nose and it becomes abscessed and elongated, then it is called "perpendicular"; if it is thick and round in the lower part, then it is called a "bubble".
But when it has been healed with what we have mentioned in the discussion, and you do not perceive any improvement, and the abscess is still present or has become subtle, then you must make an incision in the round area; but if it is elongated, and is bloody, dark in color or black, and not close to the center, then you must be cautious when making the incision, as there is a risk of harming the patient.
And when you see it as I have described, based on its whiteness and length, then make the patient lie down and hold their tongue with an instrument of the type that was mentioned earlier; place a probe into the new opening and pull it downward, making an incision with one of the two instruments that were mentioned in the treatment of two abscesses.
And it is important that you only make an incision in the area that is ready for it, without going beyond the natural boundary; if you make an incision beyond this point, you may damage their voice.
And when making the incision, use what we recommended in the treatment of two abscesses, and dress the wound until it heals.
But if the patient is afraid of the incision, then it is necessary to use cauterization without causing fear; and the method for cauterizing them should be with hot water, which you can do by placing the patient's head in your lap, holding their tongue with the instrument that we mentioned earlier, and then taking the hot water that we described in the chapter on cauterization; and apply it to the live flesh, but not too thick or thin, and use the instrument of this shape to fill the concavity.
Let the end of the instrument that holds the medicine be concave, similar to the bowl of a spoon, and place it on the tumor; then apply the instrument with the medicine to the nose, and have the patient lie on their side so that saliva or mucus from their mouth does not come into contact with the medicine inside the instrument, in order to prevent any substance from getting inside the scrotum and causing harm.
And then place your hand with the medicine over the tumor, and press it firmly for a quarter of an hour until you see that it has turned black and become numb from the bite of the medicine.
And if you wish, take some cotton and wrap it around the end of the instrument; then submerge it in the medicine, and insert the instrument with the cotton into a tube or cannula so that the cotton adheres to the inside of the cannula, and do this several times until you achieve the desired result from the cauterization of the tumor. Then leave it alone for three or four days so that it dries out and falls off on its own.
And if you find it necessary to repeat the medicine, then do so; and when cauterizing, wipe around the tumor with a cotton swab dipped in balm, and clean away any residue of the medicine from around the area; wash it with clean water, and apply an ointment on the outside, and dress the wound on the inside with bandages until it heals.
And this type of treatment is safer than incision and more cautious due to fear.
Sometimes the uvula can be cured with a method that is more subtle than cauterization or incision, which is done through sublimation in this way: take pennyroyal, hyssop, oregano, rue, Arabic zedoary, chamomile, and similar herbs; grind all of these ingredients together into a powder, and mix them with vinegar and heat until boiling. Then strain the mixture through a fine cloth so that it is properly filtered, and place it in a small container with a hole in the bottom; over this hole, place an iron instrument of this shape, which should be made of silver or iron.
And insert the end of the instrument into the patient's mouth so that the steam reaches the tumor, until the tumor becomes very swollen and obscured from view.
And then repeat the process several times until it dries out completely; but be careful not to use this treatment at the beginning of an abscess, as it may make the condition worse, and instead you should wait until the abscess has matured before attempting any type of cauterization.
But if this instrument is not available to you, then take a reed and shape it into a small funnel or nozzle at one end; place the patient's mouth over this nozzle so that the steam is directed towards the tumor and does not burn their mouth. The closed end of the eggshell can also be used for this purpose, as it will prevent the steam from burning the patient's mouth.
And this treatment is healthy and safe.
Chapter 38.
On extracting thorns and foreign objects from the scrotum, and other similar causes.
Sometimes a foreign object such as a thorn or some other cause becomes embedded in the scrotum.
Therefore, it is necessary to extract whatever is visible on the surface of the scrotum, and then carefully examine the area with an instrument held in front of the sun, while also pressing down on the tongue with another instrument; this will allow you to see more clearly what is inside the scrotum.
And whatever remains hidden inside the scrotum must be dealt with by making the patient vomit before their food has been digested in the stomach, as this can help dislodge any attached foreign objects; or have the patient swallow a piece of cabbage or lettuce stalk, or a small piece of dry bread; or use sea sponge that has been soaked in vinegar and then given to the patient to chew on until it reaches the location of the thorns, at which point they will be expelled. And take an eel and bind it with its entrails, and place it inside and slowly pull it out; or take a pork belly and insert it inside and then extract it.
But if those causes (which I have mentioned) are not available, then you should use an instrument made of lead in the following way:
And it should be a little thicker than a finger, and at the end of it there should be a concavity that you can easily insert into its (the eel or pork belly's) throat.
And it should hold its head up and make sure that it touches the bone of the throat, so that it may cause damage to it or pierce the skin or flesh with its spine, or that you insert your hand into it.
But it would be better if the patient inserts it themselves, according to their knowledge of the location of the attached cause (eel or pork belly) and pushes it downwards, while pulling up the instrument with their hand, all according to the size that has been prepared for them beforehand.
Chapter 39.
On the extraction of a leech attached to the throat.
When a leech has been treated with what we have said in the division of treatment with medicines and not with cautery, look now at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, after you have pressed the tongue down with the instrument that I recommended to you.
Then if you see the leech, remove it gently with a small forceps or delicate tweezers.
And if it is not possible for you to remove it with that, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the patient's throat, and place a heated iron in the concavity of the cannula, and do this several times (until the leech is dead and has detached from the throat) and make sure the patient abstains from water for the whole day.
And then take a horn filled with cold water, open the mouth of the patient and rinse their mouth with it, and do not swallow any cause or harm in it, and keep the water in their mouth for an hour or more with their hand, because the leech will soon feel the water.
But if it has not been removed with what we recommended, then fumigate the patient with cumin or asafoetida using the instrument that we recommended in the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this four times.
And here is another way to operate in the fumigation of that (leech), which is that you take a bowl with burning coals and cover it with a lid that has a hole in the middle, through which the end of the instrument can be inserted; then perform the fumigation from above, and place the patient's mouth on the end of the cannula, closing their mouth so that the fumigation does not escape until you are sure that the fumigation has reached the leech, because the leech will soon fall.
And if it does not fall, then you should repeat the fumigation many times, and make sure the patient avoids drinking, and consumes salty foods and garlic, and does not drink water, and it is necessary to follow this regimen.
And this is the shape of the instrument used to remove a leech from the throat when it is visible, and it resembles tweezers but has some curvature. which should be placed in the throat, and the end of it resembles a stork's beak, with a sharp edge made by filing, so that when any cause is pressed, it does not let go.
Chapter 40. (This indicates the beginning of the next chapter)
In which is summarized the discourse on abscesses and their sectioning.
Abscesses are numerous species, in many ways, according to what we remember of them, and each is discussed in this book.
And they differ in the way they burst and section in two ways, one of which is through the nature of the abscess itself, and the other is based on what we find in their moisture.
And the second method is specific to the locations in which they occur, as an abscess occurring in the head is different from one occurring in the buttocks, and an abscess occurring in a fleshy location is different from one occurring at a joint; and each of them has its own treatment through surgery.
And some abscesses require that they not be punctured until the purulence in them has matured or their healing is complete.
And other abscesses require that they be incised when they are still fresh and not yet matured, such as those near the joints, because when an abscess is near a joint, its duration is prolonged until it affects the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is near a major limb, it should be incised before it matures to avoid damaging the limb. Or if it is near the buttocks, it should not be punctured when it is immature, but only if there is a risk of pressure or infection spreading inward, causing a fistula or affecting the surrounding tissue that has not healed yet. But it is important to know the timing of the incision for an abscess, and that is when it has matured.
And you should know that it is mature when the pain has subsided and the fever has ceased, and there is a decrease in redness and pulse rate, and the swelling at the top of the abscess has softened, as well as other signs.
And it is important that the incision should be made lower than the abscess and the pus from healing the swelling (eminence) should flow out.
And the incision should always be made along the length of the flesh or body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the hands or feet, and on the sides of the arms, cords of nerves, arteries; and lastly, in all equal places where there is no reflection, because in those that reflect, use incision according to the member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to wait until the digestion of it is confirmed before making an incision, as we have said; because if you do it earlier, the body's efforts for healing will be prolonged and there may be more pus and scar tissue, making the wound deeper.
But some abscesses are punctured according to the width of the flesh or body where necessary, or according to what the member needs. (meaning the affected organ or part of the body)
And it is necessary to administer small incisions for small abscesses and large incisions and wide or many sections according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses. (meaning the size of the affected area)
And other abscesses require that the cavity be concave and opened when it is formed, as in cases of abscesses in the groin or around the umbilicus (belly button) or boils, where a pan-like incision is made at the right time.
And of those that are incised with a section having three angles, there is one in which the incision is made like the shape of a myrtle leaf, such as abscesses on the ribs or sides.
And of them (abscesses) there are those in which a round incision and crescent-shaped incisions are administered, similar to those.
But for one that is not as large (as the other abscesses), such as shallow lion-like abscesses, it is necessary to make a surface or flat incision only.
And it is necessary when the abscess is large and has already gathered much pus that you incise it but do not be concerned about extracting all the pus in that hour, having extracted a part of it, then compress the abscess again on the following day, and then extract a larger portion, and repeat this many times gradually until it is healed.
And especially if the patient is weak or a woman in childbirth, or a small child, or an old person in decrepitude, because the animal spirit is often resolved with the expulsion of pus and the patient may quickly die, so close them up (the incisions) at that point.
And pay close attention to this chapter and your incision when you puncture these abscesses, it is necessary to clean the wound and consider whether the wound of the abscess is small or a flat section, then administer some of this powder or old cotton; but if the abscess is large and there are many openings in the incision, then it is necessary to place a wick in each opening so that they heal at the same time.
And if in the abscess a piece of flesh has been cut or has been concaved in the circumference, then it is necessary to fill that with old cotton or a thread made from fabric, just as when you have taken out pans or razors, without moisture; and strengthen it for three days; and proceed with that and cure it with the appropriate dressings until it is healed.
But if blood flows during your operation, then administer cold water and vinegar in which a cloth has been soaked, and place it over the location of the bleeding many times.
But if the bleeding persists, then it is necessary to administer remedies and treatments that I have recommended in many places of this book and division. (meaning different sections or chapters of the medical textbook)
But if it is in winter and the location of the abscess is a place with many nerves, then it is necessary to apply poultices made from wine and cautery oil, and place them over those locations. (meaning the affected area)
And if it is in the summer and the location is fleshy, then it is necessary to place poultices soaked in water and oil or wine and oil, and change them every day for three days, as we have said, and then it is necessary to clean the abscess and apply appropriate dressings until it heals.
And this is what is necessary to know about the treatment of abscesses in general, but according to the way of distinction I have previously mentioned, each type of abscess has a different method of cure explained in separate chapters. (meaning that specific methods for treating different types of abscesses are discussed in individual chapters)
Chapter 41.
This chapter discusses the incision of abscesses that occur on the scalp (codena del cap).
Small abscesses on the scalp are of various types that contain membranes made for their formation and there are many kinds of them.
And of them (the small abscesses) there are nodules and some of them contain moisture similar to lime. (This text is describing different appearances or characteristics of the small abscesses on the scalp, such as nodules or containing moistures that resemble lime.) And of those that contain moisture similar to sand, and similar to them; and of those that are stony, hard.
And in the sectioning and extraction of all [of them], one should not fear, as the extension (or operation) of these does not cause opposite arching (or curvature).
And the operation in sectioning of these is to probe them with an instrument that has a shape that approaches this (?), which is called an "entromes," until you are certain that it contains [what you're looking for].
If what is contained (within) is moisture, then you should cut it with sectioning along the length by surface sectioning in this shape:
Begin the sectioning along the line of B to the line of G. Once the moisture is evacuated, then you should excoriate (remove or cut away) that which contains the moisture and leave no cause for it at all, because too often what remains returns, if any cause remains.
Then immerse a piece of cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present, and if not, in water and salt; then fill the wound with that and leave it in for another day, because with this it will corrode all that is hardened from that skin.
Then repeat the application of Egyptian ointment to the cotton and clean it a second and third time, if necessary, until you are confident that there is no remaining cause of that skin; then heal the wound with ointment until it is healed.
And if an abscess contains fatty nodes, then you should incise it (cut into) according to this form: with an incision that has the shape of a cross, and make an opening between two lips of the incision and cut through all parts (of it), and exert your strength in the extraction of the membrane that contains it.
But if your arching (curvature) is contrary (opposing), then do what I have told you previously.
And similarly, do this with an abscess that is stony (hard) in sectioning and healing according to what we have told you; and a section on a hard abscess is easier because it contains little blood and little moisture.
And sometimes there are boils of these abscesses that occur in the head, in certain men who do not have any moisture at all; which is caused by the fact that I incised on an abscess in the head of an old woman and found it to be as hard as a stone, rough, white, and unable to be pierced. And if anyone were to strike against it, they would be injured.
But in other abscesses that occur in the head, this is not the case, as with abscesses that occur on children's heads and are located at the temples, but the sectioning of all these should be surface sectioning.
And place the opening of these at the lower part of them so that the body is relieved of pus in the lower parts.
And similarly, heal these with what is appropriate for healing.

Chapter 42: On the sectioning of scrofulas that occur in the neck.
Often, these abscesses occur in the neck and armpits and groin; and sometimes they occur in other parts of the body.
And those that occur in the neck are of this type, and many of them are generated between them (lymph nodes), and every scrofula of these is within its own membrane, and just like in the glands and abscesses of the head, as we have discussed.
And the types of these scrofulas are many, for some of them are stony (hard), and some contain moisture, and some are malignant which do not respond to treatment.
Therefore, in the one that you see with good disposition upon examination, of which the color of what is evident is close to the color of the skin, and it is soft all around, and not connected to the neck nerve, nor to veins, nor to the arching (curvature), and is not prominent, then it is necessary that you incise that one with dry surface sectioning from the upper part of the body to the lower part of the body along the line of G between the line of B, and scrape that one completely on all sides, and extend two lips of the skin with an inch or with many inches if you need those, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract that slowly little by little.
And it is more caution that the vein or nerve should not be incised (cut into).
And the scalpel should not be too sharp, so that it does not fit your hand for incision, or that it disturbs the patient, and that you cut what is not necessary to incise; because if you were to cut a vein or arching (curvature) it would prohibit you from continuing with your operation. Therefore, stop in the wound with vitriol trissat or other powders that stop blood flow, tighten the wound, and let it rest so that the acuity of the abscess subsides, and soften the wound so that it begins to become putrid. When blood is cut (stopped).
And then return to your operation until you have completed it.
And similarly, ask your informed judgement if there is any remaining cause of the other small scrofulas, then incise those and clean them out.
And if it is at the root of the large vein, then it is necessary that you do not incise that scrofula from its roots. Beforehand, it is necessary to tie that one with strong doubled bile (gall) and leave it inside so that it falls out by itself without harm.
And apply a compress of old goat's wool that you have previously soaked in Egyptian paste, and treat the wound in this way.
And if you incise the entire scrofulous sore, then it is necessary for you to bring together the edges of the wound and stitch it up immediately so that no extra tissue remains.
But if you see that there is extra tissue due to the size of the scrofula, then it is necessary for you to decide to cut out the root of it and remove it, and administer stitches accordingly.
And for scrofulas that contain moisture, make a shallow puncture in the area of its maturation and place a puncture that dries out the pus from deep within, as we have said.
And then administer punctures, cauterize with fire and similar substances to corrode that which is rotten from the corruption. And when you see that the wound is already clean, then treat it with flesh-generating ointment until it heals.

On the incision of the pustule of an abscess in the armpit. (Note that "apostema" is a medieval term for an abscess, and "guolayro" is an old word for "armpit".)
The ancients recommended this incision in the pustule, but I have not seen any person in our land who has done it that way. (Note: "epilhot" is likely a typo or misspelling of "aposthemate", an old word for abscess.)
And this is the inscription of the speech of those (people). (Note: "sermo" means speech, and "inscriptura" refers to some sort of written record or description of it.)
But in men with inflammation, it is necessary to avoid extracting the pustule, since this does not bring any benefit because all the veins and arteries of the patient are here (in the armpit).
But in those who have abscesses in the mouth or armpits or ears, when the illness is not in the bone, it is necessary to make an incision in the pustule in order to avoid the danger that comes from bursting.
Therefore it is necessary to incise the pustule below three circles of the pustule or four with a small section along its length in the area between two circles where there is no cartilage, and this location is suitable for incision because it is devoid of flesh and the blood vessels are sparse.
And if the doctor is afraid, then it is necessary for him to stretch the skin of the armpit with an ounce weight and make a cut in the skin until he reaches the canal, but he must avoid cutting any blood vessels for any reason.

And now I say that in the incision of the pustule there is no fear. (Note: "seccio" means incision or cut, and "epilhot" refers to a pus-filled swelling or abscess.)
