Chapter 47.
On the treatment of male breasts which resemble those of women.
Some men's breasts become swollen as they begin to sleep and are touched, and then their breasts become swollen and resemble women's breasts, or those of Roman prostitutes, who are called "apostema" in Latin.[*](note: I'm not sure about the meaning of "lejas", so I have translated it as "called".)
And for those who have this problem, it is necessary to cut along the lunar section (i.e., along the line between points B and G), remove all the swelling, apply a plaster made of carmine medicine, suture the two lips of the wound, and care for the inside until it heals completely.
But if the breast tilts downward and softens like that of women, it should be cut in half along its upper parts with two incisions similar to a crescent moon shape, each containing the other until the end of each line, so that the larger line contains the smaller one, as shown in this figure (drawing a line from B to G). Then remove the tissue between the two lips of the wound and drain the fatty tissue. Finally, perform the suturing and administer the powder necessary for healing until it is cured.
And if you do not complete the incision as required due to the patient's discomfort or bleeding, then it is necessary to apply a dressing of sterilized gauze soaked in corrosive ointment and leave it until the dead tissue is dissolved, then cure the inside until it heals completely.
Chapter 48.
On the puncturing of abscesses that cause pain in the lower body.
These abscesses that cause pain in the lower body are of the type called "scrofula", hard, and contain a pouch-like membrane.
And some of these abscesses contain fluid, and those that contain fluid must be incised with a lunar section along this line: from G to B. Once all the pus has been drained from the abscess, pack it with clean cloth and leave it to heal for several days.
And then apply a dressing to cover it and care for it with appropriate ointment until it heals completely.
And if the abscess is of the type called "nodes" or "scrofula", then cut it as I have described in the section on scrofula.
But if the wound is extensive and likely to become gangrenous, then apply cauterization as I have described earlier.
Chapter 49.
Chapter 49: On incisions of abscesses caused by arteries or veins.
Chapter 50: On the signs and symptoms of abscesses caused by arteries or veins.
And when it is caused by a vein, the abscess is round and visible on the surface of the body.
Incision of this abscess should be avoided, especially in areas such as the armpits, groin, neck, and other parts of the body where there is a risk of complications. The incision of an abscess that is large or located in the extremities or head should also be avoided.
But for an abscess caused by inflammation of the orifice of an artery, make an incision in the hard swelling along its length. Then open the incision with forceps and expose the artery, removing any surrounding tissue until it is visible.
And then place a needle on top of it and push it through the other side, and tighten the artery with double-stranded suture in two places, which causes ischemia in the extraction of two arteries that are in the temples.
And then place your finger on the location between two ligaments with a sponge until all the blood is drained from it and the abscess is resolved.
And then administer treatment to prevent gangrene from developing between the ligaments, and care for it with appropriate ointments until it heals completely.
And if it is an abscess caused by incision of a vein, then hold with your hand what you can of the abscess with the hard swelling, and then insert the needle below the location that you have held with your hand, and push it through; and make sure that there is double thread in it as you extract it from the other side, and then ligature the abscess with a good ligament as I have told you before, using two parts of the thread with two extremities of the ligament.
But if you are afraid that the thread will be pulled out, then insert the suture with the needle below the entire abscess along the incision of the first needle and tighten the threads in four places.
And then cut the abscess in its middle so that when it is drained, you incise the excess swelling and leave what adheres to it.
And then place a cotton ball soaked in wine and oil over it, and administer the treatment which is made with hot water and ointments until it heals completely.
Chapter L: On abscesses that occur due to nerve compression.
Just as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, similar abscesses can also occur in nerves when there is a blow or excessive work, among other causes.
And it is most commonly found in the areas of the joints or the heel, or in any location where there are weak points.
And it is a severe abscess and has the same color as the rest of the body, and is located in the largest nerves, and when it is compressed with force, the patient appears to be stunned or confused.
And this abscess does not form in the depths of the body, and for that reason it is located on the surface, and it affects all parts equally without going to the front or back.
Therefore, it is not advisable to encase abscesses in joints with iron, because they will easily become constricted.
But if it is in the head or forehead, then open the swelling with a sponge. If it is a small abscess, then make an incision in it with a lancet and drain it.
And if it is large, then ligate it with a ligature, and carefully cut it out, and close the wound with sutures, and take care of it until it has healed.
Chapter one.
On the incision of an abscess, which occurs in the cheek and also in the abdomen.
There also come to a head hard abscesses in the abdomens of some people and in other parts of their bodies, which are called fungal because they resemble mushrooms, with thin edges and thick caps; and the lips of these have turned inward, and they can be small or greatly enlarged.
And I have seen one (abscess) that was in a person's abdomen and had two parts that were more like mushrooms, and there was no difference between them in whiteness or small size.
And the lips of these had turned inward and were splitting open, and there was constant flowing moisture from them.
Therefore, I incised these and found in one of them eighteen ounces (of pus). and the other one contained five ounces (of pus).
And the procedure for incising these is to consider whether the patient is moist or not, and if their skin is white, moist, and of thin consistency; then you should incise them with a broad-bladed spatula, while keeping cauteries in the fire because you will often need to use them to stop the bleeding that occurs when the pus is expelled. If blood flows, cauterize it immediately.
And if you see that the patient is fearful and timid, be cautious about making an incision with a knife; instead, take fresh lead filings and mix them with the skin, using the method we have described, and leave it in place for two days.
Then attach it firmly to the incision with a lead wire, and do not stop strengthening the large piece of lead in the skin until it is cut through and falls off by itself without any effort.
But if the abscess is of thick consistency, then there is some cause for fear and anxiety in making an incision, especially in the one that is located in the abdomen.
But it is also possible that you could incise most of it and then cauterize the area to prevent its return.
Then take care of it until the wound heals.
And be careful not to attempt to incise an abscess that is of dark color, with little sensation, and covered with thin skin, because it may be cancerous.
And I will return with a reminder about cancer related to this topic.
Chapter two.
On the treatment of a bulge in the navel.
A bulge in the navel can be caused by many factors, such as fissures in the diaphragm that are located above the abdomen and cause the intestine or hernia to protrude through it, as with other ruptures; or by bleeding from a vein or artery, as mentioned previously; or by constriction of the intestines due to gas.
But if it is caused by a fissure in the diaphragm and protrusion of the intestine or hernia, then the color of the abscess will be similar to the color of the skin, and there will be no pain, but there may be other symptoms depending on the location. But if it is caused by herniation of the intestine, then its location and symptoms will be similar to those described previously, but with more pronounced differences. And when you press on it with your fingers, it disappears and returns quickly, and it can become enlarged very easily in warm baths and with great effort.
But if it is caused by moisture, then there will be no pain and the hernia will not be hidden when pressed with the hand, nor will it be constricted or swollen.
But if it is caused by bleeding, then the abscess will appear darkened and declining in color.
But if it is caused by flesh necrosis, then the abscess will be severe, large and hard, and fixed in place according to its size.
But if it is caused by intestinal gas, then touching it will not cause pain.
And the treatment for this condition is to consider whether the bulge in the navel is caused by bleeding from an artery or a vein, or by intestinal gas. If so, then you must refrain from treating it, because as I have taught you in the chapter on abscesses caused by arteries and veins, there is cause for fear and anxiety in such cases.
But if the bulge in the navel is caused by the intestine or hernia, then you should instruct the patient to lie on their back with their legs extended. Then, using a probe, carefully examine the entire circumference of the navel and mark the location that appears abnormal. Next, have the patient turn over onto their stomach with their arms at their sides, and use a broad-bladed spatula to make an incision along the marked circle around the navel. Finally, using strong or weak suture material, carefully close the wound in a neat and orderly manner.
Then, using your finger, gently push the middle of the abscess towards the incision and insert your finger into it to search for the intestine. If you find it and hold it in place with your finger, then you can proceed to close the wound with sutures. However, if the intestine has become trapped or constricted, then you must carefully extract it from the incision and gently push it back into the abdominal cavity.
But if you find that the hernia is made up of skin or membrane, then using a ligature, tie off the excess tissue and remove it by making an incision.
But if the hernia is blocking an artery or vein, then carefully tie off the area around it and return to your operation. Then, using two needles, thread them with strong sutures and insert them into the skin in a cross shape around the abscess, making sure that they penetrate deeply. Finally, use these needles to pull the hernia in four directions, closing the wound tightly around it.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave the area open so that the flesh can heal on its own; or make another incision when the swelling has subsided and is easier to cut, and then care for the wound with appropriate dressings until it heals.
But if the bulge in the navel is due to necrotic flesh or moisture, then you should excise the abscess as we have described, remove any blood or moisture that you find, and care for the wound with appropriate dressings until it heals and the area is stable.
Chapter Three
On the treatment of cancer
We have said, in the division, of the type of cancer and in what manner it is possible to cure it with medicine, and that it is advisable to treat it with surgery so that it does not ulcerate; and we have said cancer generated in the mother's womb and caution in the cure of it.
The ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a location where it is possible to eradicate it, such as the type of cancer called "cran" which is in the breasts or in the groin and similar locations on the body that can be completely removed, especially when it is beginning and small.
But when it is old and large, it is not advisable to operate on it because it cannot be cured by such means, nor have I seen it done or heard of a successful outcome.
And the operation for cancer should be performed as follows, as we have said: first, you should prepare the patient and purge them of black bile several times, and then let blood if there is obvious congestion.
And you should also prepare the patient for the operation by placing them in a location suitable for surgery and providing surgical instruments with hooks, which are necessary; and use a concave scalpel of good quality to carefully dissect and remove all causes of the disease without leaving any remaining. And let the blood flow and do not cut too lightly, and press on the wound to express any clots, and wipe away the thick blood with your hand or with an appropriate instrument that is available to you.
But if there is an obstruction to the flow of blood due to a vein or artery, then cauterize it to stop the bleeding and treat it with other methods until it has healed.
Chapter 50
On the treatment of edema (also known as dropsy)
As we have previously discussed in the division of this topic, there are several types of edema, each with its own distinguishing characteristics, and we have also explained how to treat them with medicine.
And the type of edema that can be treated with surgery is only the one called "althitas," and it should not be confused with the types known as "timpanistres" or "yposarcha," which are fatal when operated on.

Chapter 65.
Of the treatment of intestinal hernias.

Chapter 69.
On Castration.
Know that castration is forbidden in our religion, but it is appropriate for me to mention it in this book; and there are only two reasons to do so: the first reason is so that it is part of the physician's knowledge when they are questioned about it, and they know how to treat those who experience it; and the second reason is that we often have a need for castration of other animals for our use, such as with mules, oxen, pigs, and similar beasts.
And so I say that castration is done in two ways: either by compression or by incision (cutting) into a section.
But in the one that is done by compression, the way of performing the operation is to submerge the animal in warm water until its genitals become relaxed and limp and hang down. And then take hold of them with your hand until they are relaxed and do not appear again after the procedure.
But in castration done by incision and cutting, it is necessary to hold the animal and press down on the base of the testicles with your left hand.
Then lift the suspensory ligament and make an incision on each side up to where two processes (protrusions) come out.
Then make an incision into the scrotum that you have dissected (cut open). And do not leave any tissue on the part of the kidney; instead, cut it very close to the vessels (vas deferens).
And this method of castration, which is done by compression, is better because it leaves some tissue from the testicles, allowing the animal to still have sexual desire.
Then heal the wound until it is healed.

But in women, it occurs as a single type: the labia of the female resembles the scrotum of a male, with two rounded parts that protrude slightly like the testicles of a male.

In the second type of males who have urethral opening in the scrotum, there is no treatment or surgical procedure for this condition.

And I have seen a woman in whose womb there was a dead fetus, and then another pregnant woman lay over it, and the fetus of that other one died as well. A certain man had an abscess in his navel for a long time; and it swelled until fire broke out, and he began to throw his arms.

Of the treatment of fistulas that form below.
Fistulas that form in the lower part are knotted and thick, which form near the buttocks outside or in the area of one side.
And it is a fistula or an abscess.
And when this knot is old and has dried from the moisture of white watery pus or thin powder, and sometimes these fistulas have some openings.
And these openings are known because something exits from them through egression and windiness; sometimes the patient uses egression, and often it is easy for worms to exit from them.
And sometimes these fistulas have openings that penetrate into the bladder, and into the flesh of the penis; and sometimes they penetrate into the joint of the thigh, and into the node of the testicle.
And what makes a penetrating or non-penetrating fistula known is that you insert your finger into the anus and gently introduce a thin piece of lead or iron into the fistula if there is no curvature.
But if there is curvature in this one, then introduce a thin piece of lead or horsehair into it until you feel it with your finger.
And if you do not feel it at all or make any progress due to some cause of egestion, worms, or flatulence, as we have said, then you know that it is non-penetrating, and then proceed with the treatment.
And when the fistula penetrates into the bladder or into the flesh of the penis, then the symptom of it is the excretion of urine from that one and prevention of it until the area has been consolidated with medicine.
But if it penetrates into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and causes pain in the surrounding area, then the symptom of it is that a probe can enter easily into it if there is no curvature in the bone, and there is pain in the surrounding area of the affected part; and there is always pus coming from it; and it does not respond to any medicine, nor is it consolidated with ointment.
And in all penetrating fistulas, there is no complete cure, and the treatment of these is laborious and futile on the part of foolish doctors who are mistaken.
But in one that is not penetrating and not old, healing with iron is expected, according to what I have told you and proven.
And it is that the patient lies on their back with their hands under their hips and raises their legs into the air, the thighs are inclined toward the stomach, and then gently introduce a lead probe or an iron one if there is curvature in the fistula until you know where the probe can enter.
And if the patient feels it around the anus, then it is necessary to insert your finger into the anus.
And if you feel the probe with your finger already inserted and penetrating on its own without touching it with your finger or flesh, then you know certainly that this one is penetrating; and then do not work on it, because there is no healing in it, as we have said.
But they say abscesses can be healed in some slow-healing men.
And the medicine by which there is hope for help in it is that you light a pointed cautery of appropriate size according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before, and insert this fire into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and then repeat this two or three times until you know that all the diseased flesh has been completely burned and resembles feathers of birds.
And treat that with bandages wrapped in linen until all the burned flesh has healed, and then treat it with wound-healing medicines to generate and consolidate the flesh, and if it is healed, then it is good; but if not, then it is never healed at any time by another treatment.
And if the probe enters and does not penetrate into your finger that is in the anus, and between them there is a thin layer of flesh or membrane, sometimes the fistula is in this area where it dries out the surface of the anus, then dry out the anus from the beginning of the fistula with the probe, and you see it drying with the probe, and keep it inside the fistula until the drying reaches the location where the end of the probe is, and the obstruction is released and cured through the probe.
And then clean the fistulous flesh which resembles feathers of birds and ensure that there is no remaining cause in it.
But if blood flows sometimes instead of pus when you insert the probe into the flesh, then let it be, and use a light instrument to cauterize with fire or sharp medicine, because cautery with fire has two good habits: one is burning of the diseased flesh, and the second is cutting off the flow of blood by drying out the moisture.
And treat it with bandages wrapped in linen or in horse hair until the location discharges pus, and then treat the wound with hard flesh-generating and consolidating ointments.
And these are medicines that have astringent and drying properties; when they are used, the location is restored and healed, and there is no fear of recurrence.
But if the fistula has already reached the anus and is elongated from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and search with it.
And therefore if you feel the probe and between it and the flesh or membrane there is a thin layer that is close to penetration, then it is not surgery in it but rather through faith and hope.
Which means that one of three methods should be administered to it: either cauterize it as we have said; or dry it out until you achieve the cavity so that it is possible for you to insert any instrument and perform the appropriate treatment, but do not cause any injury in drying so that you do not cut the ligament that holds up the anus, causing involuntary excretion from the patient; and treat it with what we have said, because it will be easily healed; or lengthen this thin layer and clean out the pus that is close to the anus with a probe or another sharp instrument, and then clean the fistulous flesh in the section where you can perform incision; and then make every effort to restore the entire wound with incision, and if the opening of the pus above it is not consolidated and the fistula remains open in the part of the anus, it will be easier for the patient to heal. and insert it into the vein wrapped in five veins or around them, and then insert the probe with the vein into the fistula until you achieve its cavity.

Regarding the suturing of hemorrhoids from which blood is flowing:
Hemorrhoids are of two types: they can be located inside the anus, resembling charcoal lumps, or they can protrude from the anus, resembling clusters of grapes. And some hemorrhoids are small and others are large; they can constantly bleed or only occasionally, either internally or externally, near the edge of the anus.
However, hemorrhoids that protrude from the anus are caused by a lack of moisture in the body; they can produce citrine-colored water or small amounts of blood continuously, and their color matches that of the surrounding skin.
To treat internal hemorrhoids, you should instruct the patient to squat and apply pressure until their anus protrudes and the hemorrhoids become visible to you. Then, you should sit and hold onto the patient's legs or use your fingernails to make small incisions in the hemorrhoids along their natural lines.
However, if the patient's legs are too slippery due to the moisture and softness of their skin, you should use a rough cloth or leather strap to grip them, and then extract the hemorrhoids using your fingers as described earlier. Once extracted, you can apply powdered cauterizing agents to the wounds in place of actual cautery, or follow the previously described method for cauterization if necessary. And treat the remaining hemorrhoids with the same procedure until they are healed.
If the anus does not respond to pressure and refuse to protrude, you should use a small biting probe to stimulate it and wash the area with water that has been used to clean the anus. This will encourage gentle protrusion when the patient bears down.
However, if the hemorrhoids are external to the anus, their cause is usually minor and can be treated by gently pressing on them with your finger or using forceps to make small incisions and then treating them as described earlier until they heal.
When suturing the incision, follow these steps: Take some thread coated in fig sap and insert it into a needle. Then use the needle to draw the hemorrhoids up to the edges of the incision and pass it through the other side. Next, wrap the ends of the thread around the base of the hemorrhoid, parallel to the incision, and pull tight to close the wound. Finally, remove the needle carefully.
Do this for all of them, leaving one unsutured so that any excess blood can drain from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or wax on the anus, and have the patient rest. And leave it inside until it falls out on its own, and then treat the wound with ointment or other remedies until it heals.
If the fistulas are old and unresponsive to medical treatment, you should irrigate them with a spatula or your fingernail until they become moist and the scab on top is removed, which will prevent them from hardening further. Then treat them until they heal completely.
Then, you should irrigate the fistulas with a very strong flow of water until they bleed and become raw; then treat them until they heal completely.
You should know that alamermar is crucial and it refers to red spots on the skin resembling the head of a nail, which can occur throughout the body but are more common in the lower extremities such as the feet and fingers. To treat pain caused by these spots, you should use the appropriate remedies.
Therefore, it is necessary to make an incision around the circumference of the red spot and remove it using forceps or forceps. Then treat the wound until it heals completely.
And if you wish, cauterize them according to the method described in their respective chapter.
Regarding warts, they are small, rough, round bumps on the surface of the skin that occur frequently in children.
The treatment for warts is to either cut and remove them or apply a paste made from fig sap or animal hair until they fall off naturally. And if desired, you can also cauterize them using heat or a caustic substance, as previously mentioned.
A formica is a small, swollen or large, rough bump on the surface of the skin that resembles a bite from an ant when touched, and it occurs around the body.
To treat a formica, take a quill pen from a goose or a vulture and make it sturdy. Place the tip of the quill over the formica, making sure to cover the entire circumference of the growth. Then, rotate your hand while holding the quill, using it to cut into the skin around the formica, until you reach its root. Finally, remove the formica from its place.
If desired, you can also use an iron or steel needle in this way:
The upper part of the needle should be fine and blunt, without any sharp point that could pierce the skin. This will ensure that the rotation of the needle is smooth and easy to control.
And if desired, you can cauterize the formica as described in the chapter on cauterization of abscesses using fire or a caustic substance.

And let it be pierced with many holes as it is rolled up, and the size of the space between the holes should be the width of a finger.
And insert into those holes strong bile from ten fresh livers, or around each of them; then attach the bag to it. Once the bag is placed on it, make sure it is tightly secured at the top of the patient's head between two separate bands with a strong binding, and tie the bag to each hole: The way to do this is by filling the bag with the medication, which should be warmed according to the patient's tolerance; and ensure that it is not too hot or too cold.
And let the patient be positioned lying on their back, and raise their legs with a support under them, such as a board or a hot stone. On the treatment of wounds.
I have already said in the division of the treatment of wounds what is necessary for the book, and now I will say the treatment with my advice and with medications according to their application.
Therefore, I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made from and the place on which the wounds occur.
And the causes by which wounds are often made are such as striking with a stone, or cutting with a sword or knife, or piercing with a spear, or staff, or arrow, or similar things from many other causes.
But wounds that are on parts of the body such as a wound on the head, or neck, or chest, or stomach, or thigh, and similar ones on other members.
And I am now describing the treatment of some wounds in order that you may have a rule and reasoning for treating other wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory of compound ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when you encounter a simple head wound and there is no fracture, consider the following: if it is caused by striking with a stone or something similar, and only the skin is torn and it is a large wound, and you fear an abscess due to hematoma in the patient, then you should quickly perform a venesection of the cephalic vein and do not delay. And extract blood from the patient according to their strength, unless there is some other reason preventing venesection, especially if the blood that has come out of the wound is scanty.
And let venesection be on the opposite side from the wounded area, and take care that the patient avoids replenishing their blood, wine, and heavy foods.
But if some cause prevents venesection, then let the patient eat less food and avoid meat and wine.
And place on the wound if an abscess has developed, apply a piece of cloth soaked in oil or wine that has been thickened with styptic powder.
But if you are sure that an abscess is not developing, then place on the wound if it is fresh and still bleeding, and apply the powder that I will recommend shortly, while keeping away from the air.
But if the air has already touched it, then place on some ointments until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or caused by cutting with a sword or something similar and the lips of it are not closed due to swelling, then close them with stitches as I will recommend for the suture of the lips.
But if the wound has exposed bone and tendons, but is only slightly hanging down like a flap, then cut it out and treat the wound with medications, restoring the flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to avoid foods that cause flatulence such as cabbage, beans, and similar ones, until it is healed.
And if you find putrefaction in the skin that does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all that is rotten and remove it, and treat the wound accordingly.
But if an artery or vein is present in these wounds and the flow of blood cannot be stopped with medicine, then look for the artery and if you find it not cut, then carefully cut it with a scalpel or tie it off; and if necessity demands that the previously mentioned methods are insufficient, then cauterize until the bleeding has stopped.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is light, in which case you should dust this powder on them before the air reaches them, so that they become hardened before the air touches them.
The method of making the powder is as follows: take one part oil of crushed sesame seeds, two parts dragon's blood resin, and three parts unburnt alum; mix well, strain, and fill the wound with it, pressing firmly so that it adheres well. Allow it to coagulate with the patient's blood.
And bind it tightly above with bandages and leave it alone until the wound is no longer at risk for infection, as the medicine should not be removed before the wound is healed.
And sometimes only cauterization is used when crushed sesame seeds and dragon's blood resin are not available to you.
And this procedure should be followed for large wounds when it is appropriate to apply it and bind them tightly, only if the wounds are fresh with their own blood and the air has not yet reached them.
And if the air has reached them, especially in summer, then it is not appropriate to use this powder, instead treat the wounds with what I have mentioned earlier. That is, apply ointments or dust the wounds with barley flour mixed with water and honey until they heal, and treat the wounds with other remedies until they are cured.
But if the wound is a small fracture in the bone, then you should remove it with gentle force.
And I will now discuss the treatment of skull fractures in cases where poisoning is suspected.
Of the wounds of the neck.
But if the wound is inflicted on the neck, then it does not differ in treatment from wounds to the head when they are simple.
But if the nerves or arteries in the neck are cut, then if it is nerves, one should avoid surgery on them using things that cause strong coagulation such as cinnebar and verdigris, which are copper acetate and similar substances, because these cause hardening and contraction of the nerves. And do not place any cold substance on the wound, because the nature of nerves is cold and their connection is with the brain, which is the most sensitive part of all the members.
And if the wound is being treated with light remedies, such as washing it gently with clean water, sometimes infused in rose oil or not, and applying powder of myrrh when washed with clean water, and other mild substances, and warm ointments.
But if the wound is large, then stitches should be applied or the lips of the wound brought together and treated with bandages until it is healed.
But if the wound is deep or there is pus in its lowest part, then pierce it at the most depressed point.
But if an artery is cut and bleeding occurs in the wound, then separate or tie off the artery, or cauterize it if necessary.
If the vertebrae of the spine have become rigid due to arthritis or any other cause, and the veins of the neck are safe, then sew up the lips of the wound over the spine with sutures, but do not touch the spine itself; instead align it and return it to its natural shape, and then strengthen it with proper supportive bandaging. Leave this in place for several days; and take care of the wound with ointments that have styptic and astringent properties until it heals.
If the disease has affected the bone, then percuss (examine by tapping) it, and if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all that you can; and leave what you cannot remove alone until the disease subsides, and the swelling decreases, and its pressure is relieved.
And if the disease is recent, then powder (apply) over it the powder that has been recommended to you. But if a fistula has formed in the disease, then treat it with what is recommended for its treatment in its own chapter.
If it is a wound caused by a lance or knife and there is air coming out of the wound, then know that the wound is fatal if the patient complains about having difficulty breathing.
And if it is not deep and the wound is recent with its own blood, then you should place a powder on it in the first hour, but do not press too hard so that the blood is not retained inside and returns to the heart and causes harm to the patient, instead place an attractive ointment on it, and loosen the bandages twice a day.
And if the ointment is not available, then place a cotton swab in the opening of the wound to absorb any moisture; and make sure that the patient sleeps on the wound so that what is accumulated in it can be drained.
But if three days or more have passed since the wound and there has been no occurrence of convulsions, palpitations, or pain in the chest, and other good signs are present, then you can be sure that the wound is healing; and at this point treat it with cupping glasses and other remedies until it heals completely.
But if the healing of the wound is delayed and it remains open for a long time, then you can be sure that a fistula has formed; treat it according to its own chapter.
If the wound is caused by a cut from a spear or knife and it is simple on the surface of the skin or back, then treat it with stitches if it is large or powder if it is small as previously described.
But if the bone has been affected and you have incised it, then twist the wound to extract any splinters that may be present; if they are separate from each other. But if they are not separate from each other, then leave them alone until the wound subsides and their removal is easier.
And for other wounds that occur in other parts of the body, their treatment is similar to what has been described.
About the diseases of the stomach or abdomen.
The indisposition that occurs in the stomach or abdomen is either large, small, or moderate.
And a small rupture is often difficult to repair in any other way, and I know that reduction (repositioning) of the intestines or nerves back to their place becomes more difficult if you do not attend to it immediately because they become swollen and engorged, making their repositioning difficult.
And therefore the best kind of rupture is moderate, because reducing the intestines back to their place in this case is not difficult, unlike the two previously mentioned kinds.
And know that there are four ways to suture the stomach or abdomen, but two of them are common and suitable for suturing other wounds in the body. [quar = because]
And two other kinds of sutures are suitable for other wounds but are specifically used in abdominal suturing.
I recommend that you explain and describe each one (of the four types of sutures) to me.
I say that when the wound is small and some part of the intestines has come out through it and reducing it back in place is difficult, then it can be due to one of two reasons: either because the rupture is small as previously mentioned, or when the intestines have become inflamed due to the coldness of the air. [inflacio = inflation]
And therefore when this is the case, it is necessary to scarify (make small cuts) on it so that you can insert a sponge or cloth soaked in warm water, or use a decoction of squinant, cyperus, and spearmint, and apply it to the inflamed intestines until the inflation subsides. [scalfes = scarify; squinant = wormwood]
And sometimes it is better to use water with astringent properties in order to resolve the inflammation.
And once you see that the inflammation has subsided, then moisten the intestines with water in which marshmallow and mallows have been boiled because it relieves the swelling of it with little effort.
But if the swelling persists and it is difficult to insert anything into the wound, then make a small incision in the rupture with an instrument that is used for incising hemorrhoids. [emorroydas = hemorrhoids; strument = instrument]
And the primary treatment is better when it involves incising only as much as necessary and not causing excessive drying or weakening of the tissues.
About the form of the instrument (that is used for incising hemorrhoids), let it be.
The one side of it should be sharp and curved, and the other side not sharp, with a fine and thin tip but not as thin as that of a spatula, rather slightly blunt.
And therefore when the wound is large and some part of the intestines has come out through it, then reducing it back to its place should be done in accordance with its natural shape and position if possible, because this is better. [reduccio = reduction; forma = form; loc = place; propri = proper]
But when the rupture is wide and located in the lower part of the abdomen, then have the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is located in the upper part of the abdomen, then place a cushion under their head and feet so that they are raised above the rest of their body. [cambas = thighs; partidas = parts; pus autas = higher; pus autz = higher]
And similarly if the rupture is located in one of the two sides of the abdomen, then direct your attention and focus towards that side so that the side where the wound is located is raised higher than the other. [partz = sides; auta = high; tua entencio = your intention; tostemps = always]
And this should be done in both large and moderate wounds. [aministres = administer; plaguas grans = large wounds; plaguas migieras = moderate wounds]
And in small wounds, use what you have prepared and make sure that the person administering it is holding the wound with their hand, adjusting its lips, and discovering an area of it for stitching if necessary. [ministrar = to administer; pyatados = experienced; labias = lips; descuebre = uncover]
And this is the common method of suturing: take a needle or a thread according to the size of the wound; and then hold it from the edge of the wound at the base of the ring finger, and pull the needle through one end of the wound towards the other without piercing both ends of the skin at once, using the point of the needle to penetrate between the two layers of the skin until you have joined together two ends of the wound and two ends of the thread, and repeat this process four times. [agula = needle; cantitat = quantity; amplitut = width; extremitat = end; strenh = pull; ciphac = suture material; codena = skin; partidas dedintz = inside layers]
And then pull the thread tight around the needle, and sometimes do this for two layers at once, and then bring together the two lips of the wound with proper closure; and then leave some space between your fingers and insert another needle into it, and then tie it to the first needle as before; and continue doing this with multiple needles until you have completed suturing the entire wound. [fiel = thread; circuit = path; contriccio = sewing together]
And let the needles be of moderate size between thickness and thinness, because very fine needles slightly cut into the flesh, and thick ones are difficult to insert into the skin, so they should be moderate in thickness and thinness. [insciden = cut into; leugierament = slightly; dificil = difficult]
And it is not necessary for the needle to penetrate too deeply into both ends of the skin because this may cause a slight cut in the flesh and lead to the wound opening up before it has healed completely. [huebra = open; consolidacio = healing]
And let the sutures not be too long because this may prevent the wound from healing properly.
And then blunt the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while they are sleeping, and place poultices on both sides of the sutures to hold them in place; and leave these in place until you are certain that the wound has healed completely. [pulvils = poultices; expanduts = spread out; entro = until] [translated by machine]
And this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds because even in the suturing of such wounds only one or two or at most a few needles are required. [habasta = up to; entorn = around]
The second common method of suturing is to use a needle with thread wrapped around it in fine and thick threads to stitch together the four ends of the skin and both ends of the wound in one go. [aministres = administer; sutura = suture; engual en subtilitat e grosseza = thread wrapped around the needle]
And then when you have penetrated these four ends with the needle, return the needle to its original position so that the thread is pulled from the deeper part of the wound to the more superficial part, making the suture resemble a stitch in fabric that strengthens it. [reduzeys = return; meteyssa partida = same place; retrayt = pull; pus subirana partida = higher part; sutura de drap = stitch in fabric]
And leave a space between each suture equal to the width of the smaller finger.
This method of suturing is common among humans.
And with such a method of suturing, I stitched the wound that had been inflicted on a man's stomach by a knife, where the rupture was larger than a palm and some intestines had come out around two palms from the middle of the belly, and the rupture was in the middle of the abdomen. And then I reduced it because the intestines had been outside the wound for 24 hours. [disrrumpcio = rupture; foro = outside; horas = hours]
And the wound healed in the span of 15 days or so, and I cured him and he recovered completely; and furthermore, he lived for many years and resumed his normal activities.
And other doctors had judged that he would not recover; and it was a miracle because I did not cure him with ointment, for it was in a place where no ointment or any medicine could be found. Instead, I applied cotton swabs twice a day and washed it assiduously with honey water until it healed completely. [jutgat = judged; metges = doctors; atrobat = found; mel = honey; ablucio = wash; assiduo = assiduous]
But I will describe two other types of suturing according to the account in the text.
The first type of suturing involves starting with stitching the skin from the outside to the inside.
And then when the needle enters the skin and continues along the length of the body, leaving the end of the thread attached to the needle, insert the needle into the other side from inside to outside at the other end of the incision, in the same way as before. [longetut = length; mihat = middle] [translated by machine]
And once you have made that incision, then make another incision in the same wound from the outside part to the inside part; and leave the extremity of the hip that is on this side, and make the needle penetrate in the other extremity from the inside part to the outside part.
And insert with that same incision you make in the hip in the extremity of the member that is inside, so that everything penetrates.
And begin from this same side of the wound and extract the needle that you inserted, which has penetrated, and return it to the kidney on this side with this extremity of the member that is inside; and extract the one from the kidney that is on the other side of the body.
And do that one time and another, and do that one time after another until you sew all that is outside according to this example.
And the sum of this method of suturing is that you sew with sutures made of animal gut, in such a way that you sew the hip one time from the side of the extremity of the kidney, and leave the other part open until it is completed.
But the second type of suturing, which I previously mentioned as belonging to Galen, is done in this way: you sew with a semicircular stitch, in such a way that the medical practitioner sews it, joining all parts together according to their natural correspondence; and they apply the extremity of one part to the other extremity of the member, and this is done as I have described.
It is necessary that you insert the needle in the extremity of the member at your own side, and make it penetrate to the inside part in that same wound, leaving both sides of the hip; and then turn the needle around and make it penetrate from the outside to the inside in both sides of the hip.
And then turn those sutures around, and make each one penetrate from the inside to the outside in both sides of the member that are on the opposite side.
And this method of suturing is better than the common light suture, and it is the suture that I previously mentioned.
This is Galen's technique.
But they also called it the "suture of the belly," which is corrected with two needles, that is, you insert in each one a thread, and begin with the needle that is on your side, and make it penetrate to the opposite side as in the suturing of those who sew animal skins.
And know that when there is a rupture in the middle of the abdomen, then the suturing of it is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
But the judgment of medical treatment for a disease is the same as for other diseases.
Which is caused by the fact that when you find the disease while it is fresh with its blood before the air alters it, and you return the intestines and sew it up properly, then place powder that promotes healing on it.
And if the air has already altered the disease, then place on it these types of ointments that are present to you until they form a hard crust and the threads come out, and the wound heals; and treat it in this way as with the treatment of other diseases until it is cured.
But if you do not have the medicines present, then place on it immediately, since it begins to heal and form a crust, and change it every two days as I have taught you, until it is cured, because you will not need any other medication in most cases when the diseases are simple.
But if you are afraid that the disease may communicate to the main members, then it is necessary that you soak wool from a lion in oil for boiling or in rose oil, and place it on the circumference of the areas that are between the armpits and the hips.
And if there is pain or putrefaction in the intestines, since this often happens, then apply a plaster made of wax and black styptic to it, especially if the powder has penetrated into the intestine and formed an ulcer in its cavity.
And know that the one that is in the large intestine heals more easily than the one that is in the small intestines.
And it is difficult to heal because the intestine called "gallbladder" does not accept healing from a wound that penetrates into it completely; and this is due to the large number of veins in it, and its great size, and due to the thinness of its body, and its proximity to the nature of nerves.
But if what comes out of the disease is a piece of tissue, and you find it fresh, then return it to its place according to your skill, in the same way that you would return the intestines.
But if it has been outside for some time and has turned green or black, then you should strengthen it with a thread over the place that is darkened by it, so that blood flows from it, because there are veins and arteries in the tissue.
And then insert what is other than this ligament, and place both ends of the thread on the side opposite the wound, so that it is relieved from its attraction to the sewing of the tissue and the emission of blood from the wound.
Recollection of diseases when they occur in the intestines.
When there is a rupture in the intestines and it is small, then it is possible for it to be restored in some people, because I have seen someone who was wounded in the stomach with a lance and had a wound on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old and had formed a fistula, and pus and gas were coming out of it.
Therefore I continued the treatment of it, knowing that it was not possible to heal it completely, but I stopped trying to refine it once it had healed and the place had hardened.
And because I saw that the place had healed, I was afraid for the patient that an accident might happen in his stomach; and no harm came to him from this accident, and he remained healthy in his various habits of eating, drinking, taking baths, and exercising.
And some experienced people have said that when there is a wound in the intestines, and it is small, then it should be bound in this way: take large-grained chickpeas; and then bring together the two lips of the wound and place one of those chickpeas that has its mouth open on the two lips of the wound; so that when you press on them, and close its mouth, cut off its head, because it adheres and is not dissolved.
And then place another chickpea next to the first one, and do not stop doing this with chickpeas, placing one next to the other, according to the size of the entire wound.
And then return it to its place and sew up the wound; and the heads of the chickpeas will remain attached inside the intestines until the intestines heal, and nothing bad will happen to the patient.
And it is possible that the intestines can be bound with delicate thread, which is made from animal intestines and is sewn with a needle; take one end of this delicate thread, and strip off its flesh, and then tie it to the other end of the thread, wrap it around, and insert this thread into needles and sew the intestines together, returning them to their place.
And this method of binding with chickpeas is only done out of hope and trust.
But if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the small intestines, then it cannot be bound, but only refined, and not completely healed.
Of the treatment of abscesses and fistulas.
Know that every wound and abscess that becomes old and forms an ulcer, and does not heal and constantly emits pus, but is not cut open, no matter where it is in the body, is called a fistula, and we call it "azucar".
And fistula in truth is hard swelling, white, with which there is no pain and it has a cavity like the cavity of a bird's quill; and because of this it is named curved hole, that is, quill.
And it is a moist hole in men, which discharges pus; and the moisture is easily drained within a few hours. And sometimes this moisture is thick, and scanty, and coarse, and thin.
I have now shown all those causes and the signs of them as well as their treatment with medicines in the division (chapter).
And it is appropriate that I should inform you about the treatment of fistula, which is made through surgery with the hand.
And know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body, for there are those that reach major veins and arteries, or nerves, or spleen, or intestines, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or any of the vertebrae of the spine, or any of the compound joints such as the wrist and ankle; and among them are those that are near to the main member.
And so among these fistulas, the one that is of this kind is one of the diseases of difficult healing and it does not accept treatment or care, and its practice requires hard work and ignorance.
And if any of the fistulas is not so deep as to reach those places that I mentioned and you hope for its healing, trust in its treatment and want to understand it better, then take an iron or a probe, and if the fistula follows a straight path, seek its depth with it.
But if the fistula is twisted, then investigate it with a thin lead probe, for lead because of its lightness follows the twisting path.
And if the fistula has many holes, it is not possible for you to recognize it with a probe.
Therefore, fill its holes with them, for the moisture that you use to fill it will flow through the other holes and come out from there. [**Note**: In this context, "clisterizas" likely refers to filling or injecting the fistula with a substance using an enema (a device commonly used in medieval medicine to introduce liquids into the body).]
And then investigate carefully, in any way that is possible for you to understand, if there are bones or nerves here, and whether the cavity of the fistula is deep or shallow, or if it is a fistula with many holes and lies above it all with all your strength, with your questioning, by asking the patient, and discovering the source of pain through your compression with your hand on the area; and similar signs and causes as in abscess. [**Note**: The sentence seems to describe a process of careful examination and questioning of the patient to determine the nature and extent of the fistula.]
And once you have examined all those causes with true scrutiny, then consider the treatment according to your judgment: and it is that you should now consider whether it is an apparent or nearby fistula in a healthy location, distant from joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the locations that I mentioned. [**Note**: This seems to indicate that the treatment for fistulas may depend on their location and proximity to various parts of the body, such as nerves, blood vessels, or joints.]
And now you should dry out the fistula as described earlier in its description, and remove anything that is draining from it and of rotten flesh, and whatever has been born in the opening of the flesh, or pus and similar things; and cure it inside so that it heals.
But if the fistula is of great depth and follows a straight path, then you must cut into it as much as possible, and clean out all the rotten flesh; and apply hot compresses wrapped in strong-smelling medicines and insert those into the cavity of the fistula that you have opened with an iron probe.
And do this several times until the strong-smelling medicine has eaten away all that is rotten in the cavity of the fistula, caused by corruption.
And then restore it with ointments that promote healthy flesh growth until it is healed. [**Note**: This seems to suggest that after removing the infected tissue and cleaning out the fistula, the physician should apply a medicated ointment that promotes healthy tissue growth to help the wound heal properly.]
But if it is not healed by this, then you should cauterize it as we have recommended. [**Note**: The text suggests that in some cases, cauterization with a hot iron or other heated object may be necessary to treat a persistent fistula. This was a common medical practice in medieval times and is still used today in certain situations. However, the decision to use cautery would depend on various factors, including the location of the fistula, its size and depth, and the patient's overall health and condition.
But if the cause of the fistula is bone and you are certain of that, then you should investigate it further and dry it out as we recommended, unless there is some other reason to avoid doing so due to a nearby vein or nerve or major body part as we mentioned earlier.
But if the bone is exposed and there is some corruption or blackness in it, then you should cut into it until you reach the source of the corruption and clean out all the infected tissue; and then promote healing by encouraging new flesh to grow over the wound.
And if it is not healed and discharges pus as before, then know that you have not yet completely removed the corruption; and so you should investigate further and carefully consider the cause of the problem and clean out any remaining infected tissue with your last efforts, using gentle methods to promote healing and encourage new flesh growth.
And so if it is healed, that's good; but if not, then you should know that the corruption lies deep within the body and has not been reached, and in such a case your only option is to leave it alone.
And if the corrupt bone is small or can be extracted, then you should extract it with fine forceps that are suited for this purpose.
And if there are many bones, then you should carefully extract all of them, leaving behind none due to your own weakness.
But if there are any obstacles to incision due to nearby moist areas, and there is no danger or risk involved, then you should cut the ligaments or flesh that may be present, and extract the bones.
But if you are not prepared to remove the bones immediately, then place a dressing on the wound that will promote healing, leaving the area around the bones undisturbed and allowing them to be surrounded by flesh and ligaments; keep the wound clean and avoid letting it become stiff or constricted as you perform your operation.
If you are concerned, place a compress soaked in treacle and turpentine oil, or an Egyptian ointment, or any other of the green ointments on it; for when these ligaments dissolve and the bones separate from them, the traction becomes easier.
But if it is a large bone such as the thighbone or hipbone or similar ones, and only the surface of it is affected by corruption, then cut into the surface layer until the blackness and corruption has been removed, and then promote healing of the wound.
But if the corruption has affected a large portion of the bone and has reached the marrow, then it is necessary to close the wound and refrain from cutting any further into the area where the corruption has spread; instead, promote healing and consolidation of the wound.
I recommend that you use a cushion or support under the patient's hips to aid in your operation.
There was a young man of about thirty years old who experienced pain in his groin, and the matter inside his body had moved to the area near the hip joint, causing an abscess with significant swelling, and this was not caused by any external factor.
The abscess was allowed to progress for some time due to the error of the doctors, and it grew larger, and its treatment was delayed until the hip joint became fistulized, resulting in many openings that drained pus and other bodily fluids.
Many doctors treated him for two years, but none were successful in curing him until I was called upon to help.
I examined the thigh of the man and saw the pus-filled openings from which it was draining, and his entire body had become emaciated with a yellowish tinge to his skin.
Then I inserted a probe into one of the openings and reached the bone.
And then I carefully examined all of the openings and found that they led to different parts of the thigh bone.
Then I considered my options and made an incision in one of the openings, exposing a portion of the bone, which I found to be corrupt and crumbling with signs of necrosis; it had also spread to a part of the thigh muscle, where it had penetrated deep into the tissue.
Then I carefully removed the corrupt bone and prepared the area for healing.
I believed that it was not the bone itself but rather the corruption in it that needed to be removed and discarded, which I had already done.
And then I promoted healing of the wound with consolidating medications for a long time, but it still did not heal properly.
And then I re-examined and found that the bone was still affected by corruption, so I cut further into it and discovered even more widespread decay.
I removed the corrupt tissue and performed a thorough cleansing of the wound, but despite my efforts, it did not heal properly.
And so I investigated further and continued to cut into the bone gradually and meticulously, eventually removing a piece about the size of a hand's width, including its marrow; then I used medications to promote healing, and the wound became slightly consolidated and healed.
And there was no need for further cutting or sectioning during the operation except for the weakness of his body and his fear of death, as he frequently suffered from fainting spells due to excessive bodily discharge.
And so he was completely healed, with no hardened flesh remaining in the area of the bone; his body had regained its proper alignment and vitality, and he was able to return to his normal activities without any adverse effects or harm.
But if the bone is prominent in a traumatized area of the body, then it must be cut as follows: take a ligament and tie it tightly around the end of the protruding bone, and command someone to pull on it; place a thicker linen bandage over the first one; then draw the skin taut over the bone with forceps and extend the limb so that the skin is drawn toward the area where you want to make the incision; finally, clear away the skin from the area where you want to cut in order to avoid cutting into the skin.
And place a board or stick under the bone in a suitable position, so that when you make the cut with the saw, it will not cut into the corrupt flesh.
And it is necessary that the sawing be done gradually on the corrupt spot, because if the corruption is in the concavity of the bone and not visible or palpable, the saw may cut into it from another direction.
But if the bone is corrupt and not prominent, and one side of it is connected to the other, and the corruption is in the middle or on one side, then you should expose all the flesh around it; and place a board underneath, and saw through the first section where the corruption is until the sawing is continuous with the second section.
And let the surgery be tailored to the location of the corruption, small as we have said.
And if the corruption is in the joint, cut open that corrupt joint and saw the bone at the point where it connects to the other part.
And if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, then it is not reasonable but instead an abnormality.
And if the corruption is in the arm pit of the hand or foot, it is difficult; but it is necessary that you investigate the corruption in the manner it appears to you, and that you cut open that which can be cut, and clean it in a way that is possible for you, and correct every abnormality as long as it does not conflict with veins or nerves.
