"De incisio extremitatibus" can be translated as "regarding the cutting of ends or extremities," while "de serratura ossium" can be translated as "regarding the sawing of bones." Therefore, the phrase "De inscizio extremitatatz e de la serratura dels osses" can be translated to "Regarding the cutting of extremities and the sawing of bones" or "On incisions at the ends and sawing bones."
Extremities can become necrotic or undergo corruption due to intrinsic or extrinsic causes, or when a disease is not cured by medications, and sometimes the corruption spreads to the limb that is unaffected, in which case it is necessary to cut into the member where the corruption has spread, in order to prevent death or further damage to the limb.
And the sign of one who is affected, is that the member becomes black inside and appears to be charred, or you may notice the darkness spreading inside the member until it engulfs the whole body; therefore, quickly proceed with cutting into that part.
Similarly, if the corruption is caused by a venomous strike from animals such as sea scorpions, vipers, or spiny fish, then it is necessary to proceed with incisions.
And if the corruption or strike is on the extremity of the finger, then you should cut into the finger and not allow space for the corruption to enter into the hand.
And similarly, if the corruption has reached the hand, then you should cut into it with an incision along the wrist, and not allow space for the corruption to enter into the forearm.
And if that is not possible, then you should cut into the arm at the elbow joint.
And if the corruption has passed beyond and you see it has spread around the elbow, then in that case death is inevitable for the patient. There is no other remedy or cure to be administered.
And similarly, do this for the foot when corruption affects the skin of the foot, therefore you make an incision in it to one of the toes.
And if it takes hold in the sole of the foot, therefore you should incise the entire foot. But if it rises into the tendon, therefore you should incise the calf at the joint of the tendon.
And if the corruption has already reached the tendon, then there is no ingestion but dismissal, and leave the patient to death.
The method of incising the limb or binding it is that you tighten the ligament in the part below where you want to incise, and tighten another ligament on top of the spot; and stretch a ligament by the lower parts, and stretch another ligament upon them; and separate the flesh which is between two ligaments as far apart as a finger's breadth so that all the flesh is exposed; and then let it be incised or bound.
And it is necessary that cloth be placed on all sides so that it does not touch the wound, and that for the patient there comes an appropriate dressing and healing cautery.
But if there occurs bleeding of blood when you operate, therefore cauterize the spot moderately, or place some restraining powders on it to stop the blood; and then return to your treatment until it is finished.
And then bind the affected limb with a ligature in a suitable place and cure that which is within until it heals.
I recommend to you that which happens to a man in his foot, this same accident that happened to me, which is because of blackness in his foot with scorching which was like a fire's burning.
And this corruption occurred first in his skin, extending over the entire foot.
And then that man prepared for himself likewise pus which accompanied the cure going to the limb with the vehemence of him who overcame pain and scorching from it, and he incised the foot at the joint, and it was healed.
For a long time that man suffered from this same corruption in the skin of his right index finger.
And then he came to me, and I managed to relieve him by applying remedies on his hand, in order to cleanse his body; but the discharge was not relieved and began to spread to another finger until it reached the hand.
And he asked me to incise his hand, but I did not want to do that, hoping for the relief of this discharge, and fearing rather the incision of his hand would lead to death, because the power of the illness was so strong.
And because he lost hope in me, he returned to his own country and later I heard that this man prepared himself and incised his entire hand, and was healed.
I have not prolonged this narrative except to serve as an aid for those afflicted by this illness, and it is a sign which may be understood and followed in its treatment.
On the care of sinuses and the quality of cleansing with medicines.
When an abscess forms in fleshy members and the space of the abscess is extended to such a degree that it collects pus, and then it bursts open and is perforated, and pus comes out of it, leaving a hollow cavity like a vessel, and the skin above it shrinks like thin cloth, and it has not spread to deep corruption, and it has neither affected bone nor nerve nor ligament, this is called a sinus, and it is not named a fistula.
But if the space extends to such a degree that corruption affects some member, therefore it is called a fistula and not a sinus.
And the treatment of it is that you incise the entire skin in the way it has folded over, especially when it has shrunk and become thin like cloth, and make sure that it does not stick to the location due to corruption.
But if you hope that the skin will stick and that the corruption has not yet reached in a deeper consequence, and there is some softness of flesh visible, then treat this with an enema.
And if you consider the sinus, and find that it is large, and there is fetid odor from it, then give an enema with this Egyptian medicine which consists of oil, vinegar, and juniper, receiving equal parts and mixed together in a vessel, and heated over the fire until the medicine becomes thick like honey.
And then take what is necessary from it and dissolve it in water and honey, and give the enema for the sinus, and strengthen the orifices of it, and leave the medicine in for two hours.
And then extract that with stool, and do this for so many days until the sinus is cleaned out and the bad smell disappears.
And sometimes it is given an enema of ashes and water, when this medicine is not available to you; and take the ash of wheat and pour water over it, and then boil that and give the enema with it until you are certain that the sinus has been stopped.
And if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then give an enema of water and honey with juniper juice mixed in three hundred parts, and also give an enema of wine and honey mixed together, because the property of honey is to cleanse and wash, while the wine causes the sinus to adhere, especially when the wine has a surplus of stypticity and dryness.
And when you do this several times and are certain that the sinus has healed, then give an enema with something which makes the flesh grow in it.
And take diaphoretic ointment and dissolve it in rose oil and astringent wine, or give an enema with some medicines and other ointments which have the properties that I have written about in the treatise on ointments.
But if the orifice of the sinus is narrow and cannot receive the cannula for an enema, then gradually widen it with a small iron instrument, and place in it a cloth dipped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it has been widened.
And similarly, if the orifice is wide, then bring together its lips with stitches and leave enough space for the enema cannula to be added without overflowing.
And if the orifice of it from which pus flows is raised up above, then dry that part at a lower location in order to make the pus flow into the lower part, because when the pus is obstructed by the swelling of the sinus, flesh is generated there.
And if it is not possible for you to dry the sinus in the area below the bone as you wish, then make sure that the member is prepared with a preparation which allows the pus to flow out lightly, according to what is appropriate, and without any obstruction of the pus remaining.
But the one that is over the opening of the sinus should remain in place at all times so as not to obstruct what flows from it. And so that you know if what flows from the opening is much or little, digested or undigested.
And in this, you consider the location of that cavity, whether the patient feels pain there or not, and if there is an abscess present.
And as your treatment progresses in this manner, and you see the matter that is discharged from the cavity's opening has adhered or begun to stick, then loosen it on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the dressing for a new one.
But if the cavity is deep and contains subtle and pervasive corruption, then do not be alarmed by any adhesion that forms there, for it indicates healing, as this happens in those who have a slow generation of flesh in their wounds, and it is precisely the opposite for others.
And if for many days pus has been discharged from the cavity, then know that it is not healing, and if adhesion in the cavity is slow to form, and the cause prolonged, then adjust the dryness of the medicines, and if they are wet in their substance and effect, make them as dry as a diaphanicon ointment when there is an excess of addition of fat.
The last remedy for healing is to take diaphanicon ointment and dissolve it in roasted oil, then add some crushed egg white into its substance and mix it well with that. Use this mixture.
And perform this action when there is no pus, by using diaphanicon ointment, melted until it becomes thick, and use that; or take myrrh, aloe, and wax, grind them into a fine powder over fire and place it on a cloth, then apply it to the cavity. Grind the mixture with honey until it becomes thick, then sprinkle it on a cloth and apply it.
And sometimes these remedies are administered with long aristolochia and celestial lily root (celestial lily is a type of plant) and powdered iris and centaury, and use these simple herbs or adjust them as needed, grind them into a fine powder and sprinkle it over the honey that I have mentioned; and use that.
And if the cavity is prolonged and does not heal with this treatment, then know that the corruption is in its depths and has formed a fistula in the bones or other hard members or tendons; then cure it with fistula treatment as mentioned before.
The following is about treating paronychia (inflammation of the nail fold), onychia (nail infection or inflammation), digital incisions, and finger amputations.
Paronychia is an abscess that forms under the nail of the finger or toe and can occur in other fingers as well. If it becomes prolonged and its treatment is less valued, then it can become a deeper abscess or corrupted, causing pus to discharge from beneath the nail, which can cause its decay and easily spread corruption into the bone within, resulting in a stinky odor and causing the finger's tip to rot. The color of the affected area becomes darkened.
And therefore when you have that with what we have mentioned in the division and it does not respond to your treatment, then it is necessary that you make an incision with iron through all the excess skin that has formed on the nail and cauterize the wound with that because cautery is helpful in this case.
But if the bone is healthy and the nail is also sound, but the growths of the nail are already compressing the flesh against its divisions, causing it to pierce and injure that area, then it is necessary to make a fine incision below the angle of the nail, carefully pushing back the skin and making an incision in the flesh with ease. Place remnants of the flesh on a cloth soaked in corrosive burning medicines until it has all been consumed; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
But if the corruption has already entered the bone, then it is necessary to make an incision in the bone and extract it because there will never be a cure as long as the bone is corrupted.
And if sometimes the corruption and decay spread to the finger, then you should make an incision in one of the knuckles according to the memory that is pressed there, and then cure it until it is healed.
But if the nail has undergone percussion or friction and it causes intense pain, then at first, it is necessary to bleed the patient, and then dry the nail with a sharp spatula with a transverse section from above downward, ensuring that the incision does not reach the flesh below the nail. This will prevent an intense pain for the patient and avoid causing an abnormal growth of skin in the area. Then cure it with something that alleviates the pain.
But sometimes, what is abnormal for some people can be normal for others, as it can easily become all flesh in the case of certain individuals, or become bone in other cases, or even turn into a nail.
And some are born on the sides of the joints, while others are born in certain knuckles of the fingers. But one that is born on the knuckles of the finger will not be harmful, whereas one that is born in the joints can easily become problematic.
And for those that are fleshy at birth, the incision should be light, and it is done by making a cut along its side with a flat spatula.
But for those born on the sides of the joints, the cure is difficult and therefore one should be careful with any incision in that area.
But for those born on the knuckles of the finger, it is necessary to make an incision in the flesh first and create a round cut down to the bone, then use one of the appropriate saws for this purpose, and then cure it until it heals.
But if consolidation occurs in the fingers between their joints either due to congenital factors or due to injury, inflammation, burns, or similar causes, then it is necessary to cut that consolidation until the fingers return to their natural shape.
Then place a cloth soaked in roasted oil between them to prevent easy consolidation and separate them, or place a thin sheet of lead between them until the consolidation is complete as needed.
Similarly, if consolidation occurs in the fingers with the palm, then you should dry that consolidation according to what is prepared and suitable for the shape of the member.
Regarding incisions on veins, there are varicose veins.
Varicose veins are when the veins become swollen and thick with melancholic fluids that collect in various parts of the body, especially in the legs, and more so in the legs of travelers, laborers, and carriers.
Therefore, it is necessary to administer a strong purge for black bile several times with evacuation, and then bleed the patient from the basilic vein.
But the cure for varicose veins with iron can be done in two ways: one is by incising and drawing out black blood, and the other method is raising the vein and extracting it completely.
The incision method is as follows: first, soak the leg with warm water until the thick blood in the calf has been dissolved, which is the fatty part of the leg. Then bind the leg of the patient to the upper part of the thigh using a bandage, and dry the vein in one place or two or three places with a wide incision. Finally, raise the black blood with your hand from below the calf upward toward the inside, squeezing out the amount of blood that you deem necessary for the patient to bear based on their strength.
Then bind it and command the patient to avoid foods that cause black bile to form.
And repeat the cure through bloodletting when the veins are full and this is noticeable in the patient.
But elevating them is done in this way: you should massage the patient's leg, if it has many knots, and then place it in hot water until their leg becomes red and the veins become swollen; or exercise it vigorously if a bath is not available until the limb feels tired.
And dry the skin along the vein by making an incision in its length or at the back of it near the heel or on the bottom near the toes.
And then use hooks to open the skin and scrape away the vein from all sides until it can be felt, and this should be done according to what you see in the appearance of the vein as it becomes more pronounced and turns darker.
And as you leave, and from the neck, you see that whitish vein that is the cord.
And then you place the lancet below so that it is raised and removed from the neck, and suspend the ounce (or leech) above it.
Then dry another section above that one for three fingerwidths, and scrape the skin of the neck from the area above the vein where it appears.
Then raise and make an incision in the skin of the second section at the ankle, and extract what has come out through that second incision and raise it up, and then extract what is from the third section above it.
And do that until you extract the one from the highest or deepest section of all the sections, until everything is removed, and then make an incision there.
And if it does not come out easily or rise up, then insert a needle with strong double-strength thread and tie it off and extract it, or insert the lancet below it and rotate your hand until it is removed. And be careful not to make an incision, for if it is broken, it will be difficult to raise and may come out onto the patient, causing harm.
And when all of it has been completely removed, then place a wool compress soaked in vinegar and rose oil or unscented oil on the site of the wound, and care for it until it is healed.
And if the vein is constricted and twisted with a kink that prevents it from flowing as we have said, then you must make an incision along the entire length of the twist and at the sites of constriction, and then suspend it with hooks until you can raise it up.
And be careful to avoid making an incision on the vein and to not harm it, for it will be difficult to raise if you do; use your judgment carefully in this matter.

On the incision of worms generated under the skin, and it is called cattle disease.
This disease is called in some lands among us cattle disease because it often affects cows and is a worm that is born between the hide and the flesh, and travels throughout the body rising and falling, and is visible to the touch as it moves from one member to another until it breaks through the hide and comes out.
And its generation is through the putrefaction of some humors, just as worms and snakes and earthworms and ascariasis are generated in the belly.
And it is feared for its malice, because when it moves through the body and rises to the head, and reaches the brain, it easily enters and destroys the brain, and this happens often.
And therefore when you want to cure it and remove it, this is not done unless its movement and appearance through touch is first recognized, and then the area above and below it must be strongly compressed and dried, and then extracted carefully.
And if it is lodged in the flesh and you cannot find it, then place a cautery with fire on the area where it resides until it dies, and the most feared thing is its corruption, which corrupts the location as we have said.
But if you see that it has reached the head near the brain, then press strongly above the eyebrow with strong compression and dryness on it, and extract it; and it is necessary for the patient to use cleansing of their body with medicines that evacuate bad putrid humors, and be careful not to consume foods that generate putrefaction.
On the incision of disease nafir.
This disease is called in our land nafir, and it is pain that occurs in some members, and often moves from one member to another.
I have already seen this as I will tell you. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and when I uncovered her arm, I saw a small inflammation in the vein funis of the arm, and after it had been open for an hour, I saw that the inflammation move like a worm rising, but more gently than if it were possible to see it, like silver running from place to place.
And then the pain moved from that location and entered the muscle, and remained there for an hour.
And then it moves to the other side of the body until it reaches the other arm.
And it was reported to me that it moved throughout the person's body as I had seen, and I was amazed at its movement and change from member to member. And I had seen before this in my own experience in that manner, but I have also seen many who found pain being transferred from member to member. But I did not see this in the feet as I saw in the woman.
And I did not think it was anything other than because the woman was old and had dry body and visible veins, and in her case this movement of wind was felt through touch.
And it is necessary that this backward treatment not appear in those who are delicate and have moist bodies with thin veins.
And how you want to cure it, and the patient feels this pain, then do not press on the head as we have said, but instead compress above and below gently and dryly until this constricted wind is released, and cauterize the area.
But if you do not see it with your own eyes, then cure this by inducing vomiting and releasing wind from the body, and administer foul-smelling candies and pills made of serapin and similar things.
On the removal of arrows.
Arrows are varied according to their materials and the locations in which they are found, because of their diversity that includes those with large tips, small tips, concave tips, blunt tips, those with three corners, and those with tongues; and those with feathers.
And the signs of death are when an arrow strikes it and passes through the bone and exits at the cypiac which is above the brain, causing sudden severe pain, blindness in one or both eyes, dizziness, paralysis in the limbs, inflammation and burning of the tongue, spasm and confusion in thinking, vomiting bile, speech becomes difficult and voice is lost, there is white fluid like powder coming out from the wound, and blood similar to watery discharge from the flesh.
And so if you notice these signs, then you should refrain from treatment and extraction of the arrow, unless it is outside (the body).
But the signs of an arrow that has entered the heart, when it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it is stuck in a hard object, and is not easily visible; and the movement of the arrow is similar to the pulse, and flow of black clotted blood, and there is chill in the extremities, and cold sweats, and fainting; and so you know that death is imminent.
And the signs when an arrow has pierced a lung are emission of foamy blood from the wound, and the veins that are near the neck are swollen, and the patient's color changes, and they exhale great difficulty, and they ask for fresh air.[*](note: in medieval medical texts, "fresh air" often means cold air)
And if the arrow strikes the membrane that is in the feet, and the pain then is near the lower ribs, and causes severe movement with great and violent pain and sighing, and it affects not all of the limbs' muscles.
And if an arrow strikes the stomach, then food is easily vomited from the wound, which is undigested.
And if an arrow strikes the belly and is embedded in it, then there will be a wound or tear of the skin or intestines which is torn apart, and there is no hope for a cure by extracting the arrow.
And if an arrow strikes the bladder and urine comes out of it, and there is some cause that exits outside and causes pain quickly in the patient, then you know that it is fatal.
But other parts such as the face, neck, shoulder blades, shoulders and collarbones, backbones, breastbone, hip bone, thighs and their likeness of limbs are saved according to the greatest dispositions when the arrow does not hit a vein or artery and is not venomous.
And I recommend to you what I have seen about the nature of these arrows, so that you understand through this on how to treat them.
The cause is that an arrow struck a man in the lacrimal gland of his eye near the nose, and I extracted it from the other side, leaving the fragments of the ear, and he was healed, and there was no harm to his eye. [*](note: This might be referring to an injury in the nasolacrimal duct, a small passage that drains tears from the eyes into the nose, this type of injuries would not usually cause permanent damage if treated correctly)
I extracted another arrow from a Jew, which struck him in the groin of his eye, leaving the eyelid below, and the arrow was hidden and could not be found except for a small piece that adhered to its shaft, and it was a large arrow of sharp Turkish arrows, with a lion's head on it, without ears. [*](note: This is likely referring to an injury in or near the eye caused by an arrow, which would have been a serious and potentially life-threatening wound, especially if not treated correctly)
And the patient is the Jew, and there was no serious harm done to his eye.
I extracted another arrow from a Christian man, which had struck him in the shoulder, and was an Arabic arrow with ears. And then I cut into it between two ribs, and it was already submerged in his shoulder; and then I separated it with care and extracted it, and the Christian man was healed.
I extracted another arrow from a man who had been struck in the stomach, and I thought that he would die from it; but since no cause of his condition changed after 30 days, I operated on the arrow and dug into it, and he was healed, and there was no harm to him.
And I saw a man in whom an arrow struck his back and the wound became hardened on him, but after seven years, the arrow came out of the edge of his hip.
I saw a woman in whom an arrow struck her stomach, and the wound became hardened inside of her, but it did not change her condition, and the woman suffered no harm during any of her natural functions.
I saw another man in whom an arrow struck his face and the wound became hardened and broken the arrow, not causing much pain, and similar to these cases (that have been mentioned before)
I extracted the arrow from the man of the king's nobles who had been struck in the middle of his nose and it had slightly tilted to the right side and all of the arrow was hidden.
And I was called to treat him (the patient) within three days of the arrow being shot into his body.
And then I found the wound of the arrow to be very narrow; and so I examined it carefully and could not feel anything; but he (the patient) felt a pricking below his right ear, and so I suspected that this pricking was due to the tip of the arrow.
I applied a plaster to the area, which had the power of attracting and digesting (the arrow), trusting that the wound would become infected so that the location of the arrow would be revealed to me and dry out around it.
And nothing significant happened in the wound that would indicate that the arrow had reached it; and I continued to apply the plaster for many days, and no harm came of it; and during this time the wound healed, and the patient recovered from the effects of it within several days, until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose and told me about it.
And then I applied a sharp and corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was fully open, and with care I examined it and found the tip of the arrow hidden, which was attached to its shaft.
And then I used forceps to open the wound and applied the sharp medicine until it became visible to me, the tip of the arrow, over the course of several months.
And so when the wound was large and it was not possible for me to insert forceps into it, I continued to carefully examine and think of ways to remove it with tools until one day I was able to use a well-made pair of forceps to gently extract it; and then I restored the wound.
And some doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored, and I restored it and the wound healed, and the patient was cured by complete healing, and nothing remained in them for any reason.
And I recommend to you the method of extracting certain arrows so that you understand the rule and meaning regarding what I have not mentioned, because the procedures and definitions of this art are not included in my narrative or in this book.
And wise craftsmen compare little with much; and they consider what is present over what is absent; and they discover new operations and instruments for the resolution of foreign causes when accidents occur.
And so I say that arrows are not easily removed from the members in which they are embedded, but rather only in two ways: either by attraction to the location where they are embedded, or by opposition to the other side.
And the one that is removed by the location where it entered, or an arrow in a fleshy area, can be drawn out and removed.
And if it does not obey the incision of the hour when cut, then it is necessary to leave it in for several days until the flesh around it softens and the attraction to it is relieved, making its removal easier.
And similarly if it is embedded in bone and does not obey your incision, then leave it in for several days and attempt to remove it with attraction and motion each day, and it will eventually come out.
And if it does not obey your incision after several days, then you must perforate the circumference of the arrow in the bone from all sides with a subtle awl until the location is widened by the arrow, and extract it.
But if the arrow is hidden within the body and is not detectable by touch, then inquire and search for it carefully, and if you can feel it, then draw it out with suitable instruments that are appropriate for extracting it.
And if you cannot reach it due to the constriction of the wound and the length of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then make an incision in the wound until it is widened and it is possible to extract the arrow.
And if it is in the ears and is held by them, then you should release the flesh that it is embedded in from all sides with all the skill that you can muster; and be clever about how to do so, if you cannot remove the flesh from the breakage of the ears or twisting of those that obey.
And when you administer the removal of an arrow in any location where it may be, then use twisting of your hand with forceps on all sides so that it obeys; and do so with subtlety and delicacy so that the arrow is not broken and made difficult to extract.
And if you cannot do so within your allotted time, then leave it in for several days until the surrounding tissue becomes stronger, and then try again because by then it will be relieved. But if there is an opposing flow of blood, then you should administer what we have said regarding treatment in its chapter.
And be careful with your incision of veins or nerves, or tendons, and use all means at your disposal to extract the arrow; and do so with ease and calmness and patience and steadiness, as I have recommended to you.
And therefore, extract the arrow in such a way that the patient is positioned according to the figure that you should have used when casting the arrow into them, because this is more beneficial. But if that is not possible for you, then use what is possible through figures.
But arrows that are removed in the opposite direction from which they entered, or that have already proceeded some part towards the outside parts, or cause swelling in the extremity of the arrow due to feeling in the part above the proper bone and sometimes protruding; then you should dry over it, and let the incision be according to the amount that can be grasped by forceps, and then pull it out because it is easy to remove.
But if it is retained in the bone, then you should twist the flesh in the opposite direction until the arrow emerges from the bone, and expand it as it enters, and then extract it.
And if not, leave it in for several days and then try again until it comes out.
And if the shaft of the arrow is still inside, then you should push it out with it.
But if the shaft has fallen and you want to apply pressure, then insert it in, if it is blunt, with a hollow instrument so that it enters the concavity of it into the tip of the arrow and then push it out with it.
But if the arrow is concave, then you should push it out with a strong instrument entering it because the arrow will be relieved by that.
And if the arrow is poisoned, then you must curve all the flesh in which it is located, if it is possible for you to do so, and then cure it with what is necessary.
And if the arrow enters the foot, or the stomach, or the bladder, or the ribs, and is close enough that you can touch it with your probe, and it is possible for you to dry over it, then do so, and be careful not to cut into veins or nerves, and extract it, and if necessary cauterize the wound, and cure it until it heals.

On bloodletting from veins.
The veins that are commonly used for bloodletting are usually the following thirty: of which sixteen are in the head: There are two pulsatile veins near the ears, which are called "templars"; there are two herbal veins that are visible in the temples; and there are two tearful veins located in the inner corners of the eyes, known as "aspicientz". Additionally, there is a vein prepared at the center of the forehead, and another vein located at the tip of the nose. There are also two jugular veins in the neck; and two veins in each lip, one above and one below. These last four veins are called "angelic" veins; and there are two veins located beneath the tongue. But the veins that are commonly bled in the arms are five: There are five veins that are commonly bled in the arms, one of which is a cephalic vein and is located near the wild artery; this vein is known as "the vein of the head," and it is small and weak, and consists of a branch from the basilic vein and another branch from the cephalic vein. This vein is also called "the vein of the entire body" by the people, and the basilic vein is the one that runs along the domestic artery and is called "citillar," and is known to the common folk as "the belly vein." The funis of the arm is located above the elbow and is bled at this location; it is also called the "arm vein." The salvatella is a vein that runs between the auricular artery and the smallest finger, and has two branches.
And in the foot and leg there are three veins: one of these is located below the curvature of the shin bone near the wild artery; the second is saphenous, and its location is below the calf muscle near the domestic artery; the third is sciatic, and its location is below the calf muscle near the wild artery. Additionally, there are other similar veins in the leg.
The benefit of bloodletting from the veins near the ears is that it helps with ancient cases of catarrh, migraines, scabies, and old ulcers of the head:
The recommended way to perform bloodletting from the veins near the ears is as follows: gently shave the patient's head, and vigorously rub their head in the occipital region where both veins are located using a wide cloth with good friction. Then, firmly wrap the patient's neck with a band so that both veins are visible and located near the ears on two depressed areas of the head. Next, use your finger to locate these veins, and if you feel their pulse beneath your finger, then you have found them.
Then you take the incisive knife, and insert it under the vein in the elbow until the phlebotomist reaches the bone: Then raise your hand with the vein and elbow towards the upper parts, and make an incision in the vein using an incisive cut: And let the length of the incision be the length of two fingers, or thereabouts; and let blood flow from it as much as you desire:
Then apply pressure with your fingertips and leave it in place until it heals:
And I have previously discussed in the beginning of this book the incision and cauterization of these:
But the benefit of bloodletting from the two arteries in the temples is that it helps with ancient and stubborn migraines, as well as chronic eye diseases and acute cases of fluid buildup in the feet:

Of cupping and the qualities of using those.
Cups are made from horn, or from glass, or from clay.
And cupping therapy is done in two ways: one is with scraping and the extraction of blood, and the other is without scraping.
And this cupping therapy that is done without scraping is performed in two ways: either with fire or without fire.
And the cups that are administered with scraping and bloodletting are applied to 14 locations on the body, of which one is the place where cups are placed, and it is the back of the head; another location is at the base of the neck in two parts; cups are also placed under the chin below the jawbone and away from the mouth; two cups are placed on the shoulder blades; cups are applied to the lower abdomen above the pubic bone; cups are placed on both sides of the spine, one cup for each rib; and cups are placed on both ankles and knees.
And cupping therapy does not extract blood from large veins, but rather from small scattered veins in the flesh, and therefore it does not have the same effect as bloodletting; furthermore, it is not necessary for cupping therapy to be performed with or without fire in any disease caused by congestion until the body has been fully evacuated.
But if necessity requires cupping therapy for illness or chronic conditions, it should be administered at any time at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, as well as in the middle and at various times.
And therefore when any of these causes are present, particularly in the third or middle of the month, it is recommended that cupping therapy be performed at least two or three hours after sunrise.
And the benefit of cupping therapy on the neck is that it alleviates heaviness in the head and swelling in the eyes, but it is necessary for this to be accompanied by evacuation of the entire body.
And this cupping therapy should be performed at the location of bloodletting from the cephalic vein.
It is not permitted to perform cupping therapy on those who have recently experienced sexual activity or those with a cold, as this can cause great harm.
And therefore, cupping therapy should not be performed on the elderly or those with frail bodies, as they may experience negative effects.
But for the one who is continuously lying above them, a forgetfulness is made; and therefore it is necessary that you instruct the cuerer to place his hand a little below the cupping glass at the edges, in order to prevent the creation of forgetfulness.
